جس نے مسلمان کو خطا قتل کر دیا یا ایسے حربی کو قتل کیا جو دار الاسلام میں مسلمان ہو چکا تھا دیت کس پر لازم ہے
و مَنْ قَتَلَ مُسْلِمًا خَطَأَ لَا وَلِيَّ لَهُ أَوْ قَتَلَ حَرْبِيًّا دَخَلَ إِلَيْنَا بِأَمَانٍ فَأَسْلَمَ فَالدِّيَّةُ عَلَى عَاقِلَتِهِ لِلْإِمَامِ وَ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَة لِأَنَّهُ قَتَلَ نَفْساً مَعْصُومَةً خَطَأَ فَيُعْتَبَرُ بِسَائِرِ النُّفُوسِ الْمَعْصُومَةِ وَمَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ لِلْإِمَامِ أَنَّ حَقَّ الْأَخْذِ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا وَارِثَ لَهُ

ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے ایسے مسلمان کو خطا قتل کر دیا جس کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے یا ایسے حربی کو قتل کر دیا جو امان لے کر ہمارے یہاں داخل ہو کر مسلمان ہو گیا تھا ۔ تو اس قاتل کے عاقلہ ( قاتل کی مددگار برادری ) پر واجب ہوگا کہ اس مقتول کی دیت امام المسلمین کو ادا کر دے اور اس قاتل پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایک بے گناہ کو خطا قتل کیا ہے اس لئے اس کا قیاس ہر ایسے شخص پر ہوگا جو معصو اور بے گناہ ہو یعنی شرعا قتل سے محفوظ ہو ۔ اس میں امام کے پاس جمع کرنے کا جو حکم دیا ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس دیت کے وصول کرنے کا حق صرف امام کو ہوگا کیونکہ اس مقتول کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ حکم صرف اسی صورت میں ہوگا جبکہ اس نے خطا قتل کیا ہو۔ اگر عمد قتل کر دیا امام کو قتل اور دیت کا اختیار ہے
وَ إِنْ كَانَ عَمَدًا فَإِن شَاءَ الْإِمَامُ قَتَلَهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ الدِّيَةَ لِأَنَّ النَّفْسَ مَعْصُومَةُ وَالْقَتْلُ عَمَد وَ الْوَلِيُّ مَعْلُوم وَهُوَ الْعَامَّةُ أَو السُّلْطَانُ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ السُّلْطَانُ وَلِى مَنْ لَا وَلِى لَهُ وَقَوْلُهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ الدِّيَةَ مَعْنَاهُ بِطَرِيقِ الصُّلْحُ لِأَنَّ مَوْجَبَ الْعَمَدِ وَ هُوَ الْقَوَدُ عَيْنًا وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الدِّيَةَ أَنْفَعُ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَة مِنَ الْقَوْدِ فَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ وِلَايَة الصُّلْحِ عَلَى الْمَالِ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَعْفُوَ لِأَنَّ الْحَقَّ لِلْعَامَّةِ وَوِلَايَتُهُ نَظَرِيَّةُ وَلَيْسَ مِنَ النَّظَرِ إِسْقَاطُ حَقِّهِمْ مِنْ غَيْرِ عِوَضٍ
On whom is diyah obligatory for one who accidentally kills a Muslim who has no heir, or who kills a harbi who entered to us with aman and then became Muslim: Whoever kills a Muslim accidentally who has no heir, or kills a harbi who entered to us with aman and then became Muslim – then the diyah is upon his ‘aqila for the imam, and upon him is kaffarah. Because he killed an inviolable life accidentally, so he is analogized to all other inviolable lives. The meaning of his saying 'for the imam' is that the right to take it belongs to the imam, because he has no heir. Translation: And if someone accidentally killed a Muslim who has no heir, or killed a harbi who entered our land with aman and then became Muslim, then upon the killer's ‘aqila (supporting clan) it is obligatory to pay the diyah of the deceased to the imam al-muslimin, and upon the killer is kaffarah. Because he killed an innocent person accidentally, so he is analogized to every such person who is inviolable and innocent, i.e., legally protected from killing. The ruling that the diyah goes to the imam means that the right to receive it belongs only to the imam, because the deceased has no heir. This ruling only applies when he killed accidentally. If he killed intentionally, the imam has the option of execution or diyah. And if it was intentional, then if the imam wishes, he kills him, and if he wishes, he takes the diyah. Because the life is inviolable and the killing is intentional, and the guardian is known – it is the general public or the sultan. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The sultan is the guardian of one who has no guardian.' And his saying 'and if he wishes, he takes the diyah' means by way of sulh (compromise), because the necessary consequence of intentional killing is qisas itself. This is because diyah is more beneficial in this case than qisas, so for this reason he has the authority to make sulh for wealth. He does not have the right to pardon (without compensation), because the right belongs to the general public, and his authority is discretionary, and it is not in their interest to forfeit their right without compensation.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah provides the ruling for two specific cases of accidental killing: (1) a Muslim who has no known heir, and (2) a harbi who entered Dar al-Islam with aman (safe passage) and then converted to Islam, but was later killed accidentally. In both cases, the diyah is obligatory on the killer's ‘aqila (the male relatives who normally help pay blood money) and is to be given to the imam (ruler of Muslims), because the deceased has no heir to receive it. Additionally, the killer must perform kaffarah (expiation) because the life was inviolable. The passage then addresses intentional killing of such a person: the imam has the choice to execute the killer (qisas) or to take diyah by way of sulh (compromise). The imam cannot simply pardon without compensation because the right to punishment belongs to the public (al-‘ammah), and his authority is exercised in their best interest. The hadith 'The sultan is the guardian of one who has no guardian' (narrated from the Prophet) is cited as the basis for the imam's authority. The passage emphasizes that taking diyah is more beneficial than qisas in this situation, so the imam may choose it via sulh, but he cannot waive the right entirely without receiving something in return.

Key Terms
عاقلة (‘āqilah): The male paternal relatives of the killer who collectively pay diyah for accidental killings.
سلطان (sulṭān): The Muslim ruler or governing authority who acts as guardian for those without a legal heir.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise or settlement whereby the imam accepts diyah in lieu of qisas, with consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, for the intentional killing of a Muslim with no heir, what action is the imam permitted to take?
A) He must execute the killer (qisas) with no alternative.
B) He may choose to execute the killer or take diyah by way of sulh.
C) He can pardon the killer without any compensation.
D) He can only take diyah (blood money) from the killer.

Key Takeaway
For an heirless Muslim or a converted musta'min killed accidentally, diyah goes to the imam; for intentional killing, the imam may choose qisas or accept diyah via sulh.

Hanafi Classification of 'Ushr and Kharaj Lands
Defines geographical boundaries for 'ushr and kharaj lands based on historical and legal criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between 'ushr and kharaj lands according to the Hanafi school, state the geographical boundaries, and explain the legal basis from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Arab lands are 'ushr; non-Arab conquered lands are kharaj — the distinction hinges on whether the inhabitants could be left in disbelief.

This passage from the Hidayah opens the chapter on 'Ushr and Kharaj by defining the two categories of land: 'ushr land (tithe on produce) and kharaj land (land tax). The author clarifies that 'ushr is discussed first because it has elements of worship. He then defines the geographical boundaries: all Arab lands (from al-'Adhayb to Yemen, Mahrah, and the border of Syria) are 'ushr lands; the Sawad of Iraq and other conquered territories like Egypt and Syria are kharaj lands. The proof is drawn from the practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, especially the consensus (ijma) under Caliph 'Umar when imposing kharaj on the Sawad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two land categories
Recognize that the passage defines two types of land: 'ushr land (ard 'ushr) and kharaj land (ard kharaj). Understand that each is subject to a different tax: 'ushr (one-tenth of produce) or kharaj (a land tax).
2
Define the geographical boundaries
Note that Arab lands are defined as the area from al-'Adhayb to Aqdi Hajar in Yemen, to Mahrah, and to the border of Syria. The Sawad is defined from al-'Adhayb to 'Aqabat Hulwan, from al-Tha'labah (or al-'Alt) to 'Abbadan.
Al-'Adhayb is a place near Kufa and serves as the boundary point between Arab and non-Arab lands.
3
Understand the condition for kharaj
The passage states that the condition for imposing kharaj is that the inhabitants must be left on their disbelief (kufr). This was the case for the Sawad of Iraq, Egypt, and Syria, where the non-Muslim inhabitants paid kharaj and continued to practice their religion.
4
Explain why Arab lands cannot be kharaj
Arab polytheists were not given the option to remain in disbelief; they were offered only Islam or the sword. Therefore, the condition for kharaj could not be met, and their lands became 'ushr lands.
This is a distinctive Hanafi reasoning based on the early conquest policy.
5
Locate the proof (dalil)
The passage cites the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs: they never took kharaj from Arab lands. Moreover, when 'Umar conquered the Sawad, he imposed kharaj with the consensus of the Companions, and similarly on Egypt and Syria. This establishes the rule through ijma.
The dalil is zanni in transmission and meaning but is accepted as a binding precedent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْعُشْرِ وَ الْخَرَاجِ
ترجمہ باب عشر اور خراج کے بیان میں مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے پہلے ذمی ہو جانے کے اسباب بیان کر کے ذمی پر وظائف مالیہ بیان فرمائے۔ یعنی اس کی زمین اور اس کی ذات پر خراج مقرر کرنا ہے۔ اور خراج کسی اصول کے ساتھ مقرر ہوتا ہے آئندہ ذکر کیا جائے گا ۔ اور یہ زمین کا لگان محصول گھروارہ ہے اور اس زمانہ میں جو ٹیکس لیا جاتا ہے وہ عشر اور خراج دونوں سے علیحدہ ہے۔ عشر میں صرف پیداوار کا دسواں حصہ ہے ۔ چونکہ اس عشر میں عبادت کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں اس لئے عشر کو پہلے بیان کیا ہے۔ مگر جس زمین پر عشر اور جن لوگوں پر خراج لازم ہوتا ہے اسے پہلے جاننا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے مصنف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے ذکر فرمایا ہے ۔ بَابُ الْعُشْرِ الخ
قَالَ أَرْضُ الْعَرْبِ كُلُّهَا أَرْضُ عُشْرٍ وَهِيَ مَا بَيْنَ الْعَذَيْبِ إِلَى أَقْضِي حَجَرٍ بِالْيَمَنِ بِمَهْرَةَ إِلى حَدِ الشَّامِ وَالسَّوَادُ أَرْضُ خَرَاجِ وَهُوَ مَابَيْنَ الْعَذَيْبِ إِلى عَقَبَةَ حُلُوَانِ وَمِنَ الثَّعْلَبَةِ وَيُقَالُ مِنَ الْعَلْتِ إِلَى عَبَّادَانَ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَالْخُلَفَاءَ الرَّاشِدِينَ لَمْ يَأْخُذُوا الْخَرَاجَ مِنْ أَرَاضِي الْعَرَبِ وَلِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْفَى فَلَا يَثْبُتُ فِي أَرَاضِهِمْ كَمَا لَا يَنْبُتُ فِى رِقَابِهِمْ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ وَضْعَ الْخَراجِ مِنْ شَرْطِهِ أَنْ يُقَرَّ أَهْلُهَا عَلَى الْكُفْرِ كَمَا فِي سَوَادِ الْعِرَاقِ وَمُشْرِكُوا الْعَرَبِ لَا يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُمْ إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ وَالسَّيْفُ وَعُمَرُّ حِيْنَ فَتَحَ السَّوَادَ وَضَعَ الْخَرَاجَ عَلَيْهَا بِمَحْضَرِ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ وَوَضَعَ عَلى مِصْرَ افْتَحَهَا عَمْرُو بْنُ الْعَاصِ وَكَذَا اجْتَمَعَتِ الصَّحَابَةَ عَلَى وَضْعِ الْخَرَاجِ عَلَى الشَّامِ
Chapter of 'Ushr and Kharaj. Translation: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) first mentioned the causes of becoming a dhimmi and explained the financial obligations upon the dhimmi, i.e., kharaj is to be imposed on his land and poll tax on his person. How kharaj is assessed will be mentioned later. Land tax (lagan) is a government revenue and is separate from both 'ushr and kharaj. 'Ushr is only one-tenth of the produce. Because 'ushr has elements of worship, it is mentioned first. But it is necessary to first know on which land 'ushr and on which people kharaj are obligatory. Therefore, the author mentions: He said: All the land of the Arabs is 'ushr land, and it is what lies between al-'Adhayb to Aqdi Hajar in Yemen, to Mahrah, to the border of Syria. And the Sawad is kharaj land, and it is what lies between al-'Adhayb to 'Aqabat Hulwan, and from al-Tha'labah, and it is said from al-'Alt to 'Abbadan. This is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs did not take kharaj from the lands of the Arabs, and because it is like the fay' (booty), so it is not established on their lands just as it is not established on their persons. And because the condition for placing kharaj is that its inhabitants are left on disbelief, as in Sawad of Iraq, and the polytheists of the Arabs are not accepted from them except Islam or the sword. And 'Umar, when he conquered the Sawad, placed kharaj on it in the presence of the Companions, and placed on Misr which 'Amr ibn al-'As conquered, and likewise the Companions agreed on placing kharaj on Syria.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling that begins the chapter on 'Ushr (tithe) and Kharaj (land tax). The Urdu introduction explains that the author first discusses dhimmi obligations, then turns to land taxation. 'Ushr is a one-tenth tax on produce and has elements of worship, so it is discussed first. The matn then defines two categories of land: all Arab lands (from the place called al-'Adhayb to Yemen, Mahrah, and the border of Syria) are 'ushr lands, meaning that only 'ushr is levied on them. The Sawad (the fertile region of Iraq) and other conquered lands like Egypt and Syria are kharaj lands, where kharaj is imposed. The proof given is that the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs never took kharaj from Arab lands, and this is because kharaj is a levy that requires the inhabitants to remain in disbelief (as the condition for its imposition is that the land is conquered and its people are left on their religion, paying kharaj). Since the polytheist Arabs were given only the choice of Islam or death (sword), they could not be left on disbelief; hence kharaj could not apply to them. The Caliph 'Umar imposed kharaj on Sawad with the consent of the Companions, and similarly on Egypt and Syria. The Urdu commentary further clarifies that the modern land tax is different from both 'ushr and kharaj.

Key Terms
أرض عشر (ard 'ushr): Land on which 'ushr (one-tenth of produce) is levied; includes all Arab lands as defined.
أرض خراج (ard kharaj): Land on which kharaj (land tax) is levied; includes Sawad of Iraq, Egypt, Syria, etc.
العذيب (al-'Adhayb): A place near Kufa, used as a boundary between Arab and non-Arab lands.
السواد (al-Sawad): The fertile agricultural region of Iraq, from the southern border near 'Abbadan to the north near Hulwan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are Arab lands considered 'ushr lands rather than kharaj lands?
A) Because the Prophet and Caliphs did not take kharaj from them
B) Because Arab lands are less fertile
C) Because the inhabitants were all Muslims
D) Because 'ushr is easier to calculate

Key Takeaway
Arab lands are 'ushr because kharaj requires inhabitants to remain in disbelief, which was impossible for Arab polytheists.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Arab Lands Are 'Ushri: Proof from Prophetic Practice
Ruling with proof: Arab lands are 'ushri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies the entire Arabian Peninsula as 'ushri land and distinguish it from kharaji land using the proof of prophetic practice and caliphal consensus.

Core Idea
Arab lands are 'ushri because neither the Prophet nor the caliphs ever imposed kharaj on them — a precedent that determines tax classification.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the entire Arabian Peninsula is 'ushri land, subject to 'ushr rather than kharaj. The text presents the geographical boundaries and then provides evidence from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, along with reasoning based on the treatment of Arab lands as spoils. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying the land tax rules in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage and note the explicit statement that the entire land of Arabia (from 'Adhib to the stone of Mahrah in length, and from the flowing sands to Syria in width) is 'ushri. Recognize the defined boundaries.
The boundaries are traditional; modern political divisions do not affect the ruling.
2
Contrast with kharaji land
The passage contrasts Arab lands with Sawad Iraq, which is explicitly called kharaji. Note that the condition for kharaj is that the original inhabitants remain on their land, as happened in Sawad, Egypt, and Syria.
This contrast highlights the unique status of Arab lands.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The primary evidence is that the Prophet and the caliphs never took kharaj from Arab lands. This practical indicator establishes a precedent.
The proof is from Sunnah (practice) and consensus (ijma) of the Companions.
4
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Arab lands are treated like spoils (fay'), so kharaj is not applicable. Additionally, the condition for kharaj — that inhabitants remain on their land — does not apply to Arab polytheists, who are given only Islam or the sword.
This reasoning shows why the classification is not arbitrary.
5
Note the implications for other conquered lands
The Companions imposed kharaj on Sawad, Egypt, and Syria, indicating that those lands are not 'ushri. This supports the rule that only Arab lands are 'ushri by default.
The consensus (ijma) of the Companions on these cases strengthens the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم ترجمہ عرب کی پوری زمین عشری ہے۔ جو عذیب سے لے کریمن میں مہرہ کے پتھر تک ہے۔ ( یہ اس کی لمبائی کی حد ہے۔ اور چوڑائی میں ریگ رواں سے لے کر ) شام کی حد تک ہے۔ اور سواد عراق کی زمین خراجی ہے جو عقبہ حلوان تک ( چوڑائی ) میں ہے۔ اور تعلبہ سے لے کر اور کہا جاتا ہے کہ علث سے لے کر عبادان تک (لمبائی میں ) ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ اور خلفاء راشدین نے عرب کی زمین سے خراج نہیں لیا ہے۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ وہ فی و غنیمت کے حکم میں ہے۔ لہذا عرب کی زمینوں میں خراج ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے عرب والوں کی ذات اور گردن میں جزیہ لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ خراج مقرر کرنے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ اس ملک والوں کو ان کے اپنے ملک میں حسب سابق چھوڑ دیا گیا ہو ۔ جیسے کہ سواد عراق میں ہوا۔ مگر مشرکین عرب سے اسلام یا تلوار سے فیصلہ ہوگا اس کے علاوہ تیسری صورت نہ ہوگی اور حضرت عمرؓ نے جب سواد عراق کو فتح کیا تو صحابہ کرام کی موجودگی میں اس ملک پر خراج مقرر کر دیا۔ اور جب حضرت عمرو بن العاص نے مصر فتح کیا تو اس پر خراج مقرر کیا۔ اسی طرح ملک شام پر خراج لازم کرنے میں صحابہ کرام نے اجماع کیا ہے۔
Book of Siyar. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 7. Translation: The entire land of Arabia is 'ushri. From 'Adhib to the stone of Mahrah in Yemen (this is its length limit). And in width from the flowing sands to the border of Syria. And the land of Sawad Iraq is kharaji, which is from 'Aqaba Halwan in width, and from Ta'labah to, and it is said from 'Alth to 'Abadan in length. Its proof is that the Messenger of Allah and the Rightly Guided Caliphs did not take kharaj from the land of Arabia. Also because it is in the ruling of spoils. Therefore, kharaj will not be established in the lands of Arabia, just as jizyah is not obligatory upon the persons and necks of the Arabs, because the condition for imposing kharaj is that the people of that country are left in their lands as before, as happened in Sawad Iraq. However, the polytheists of Arabia will be decided by Islam or the sword; there is no other case. And when Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) conquered Sawad Iraq, in the presence of the Companions, he imposed kharaj on that land. And when Amr ibn al-As conquered Egypt, he imposed kharaj on it. Similarly, the Companions had consensus on making kharaj obligatory in Syria.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is an Urdu commentary explaining the classification of Arab lands as 'ushri. The author first defines the boundaries of Arabian lands and states that all are 'ushri. Then he provides the proof: the Prophet and caliphs never imposed kharaj on Arab lands, indicating their status as 'ushri. The reasoning is that Arab lands are treated like spoils (fay'), and thus kharaj is not applicable. He also notes that the condition for kharaj is that the inhabitants remain on their land, which occurred in Sawad Iraq. The commentary also mentions the consensus of the Companions regarding kharaj on conquered lands like Sawad, Egypt, and Syria. The Hanafi position is that the entire Arabian Peninsula is 'ushri land.

Key Terms
عشری (ʿushrī): Land subject to a one-tenth tax on produce (ʿushr) because its inhabitants are Muslims or the land was conquered and divided among the fighters.
خراجی (kharājī): Land subject to a land tax (kharaj) because it was conquered and left in the hands of non-Muslim inhabitants who retain ownership.
سواد (sawād): The fertile agricultural region of Iraq around the Tigris and Euphrates, conquered during the caliphate of Umar.
فی (fay'): Spoils of war (especially land) that come to Muslims without a military expedition; in this context, Arab lands are treated as fay'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of the land of Arabia?
A) Kharaji
B) 'Ushri
C) Both depending on the ruler
D) It is not taxed

Key Takeaway
The entire Arabian Peninsula is 'ushri land because the Prophet and caliphs never imposed kharaj on it, establishing a binding precedent.

Ownership of Sawad Iraq Lands
Ruling with proof on land ownership after conquest by force

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sawad Iraq lands and explain the proof from the imam's discretion in conquest by force.

Core Idea
Conquered land by force remains owned by its inhabitants; the imam may impose kharaj but ownership stays.

This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi distinction: when land is conquered by force (ʿanwatan), the imam has the option to leave the original inhabitants and impose a land tax (kharaj). This preserves their ownership, meaning they can sell the land and dispose of it freely. The ruling is based on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, particularly ʿUmar's treatment of Sawad Iraq. Understanding this helps you see how Hanafi fiqh balances state interests with property rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal object
The passage rules on the ownership status of Sawad Iraq lands. What exactly is being addressed? It is the permissibility of the inhabitants selling and transacting in their land.
The act is not a ritual act but a property transaction.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The land is owned by its inhabitants, and their sale and disposal are valid (sahih).
This is the clear position of the Hanafi school.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is that the imam, when conquering by force, has the option to leave the inhabitants and impose kharaj. This option shows that the land does not automatically become state property.
The passage references that this was already discussed in the chapter on division of spoils.
4
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The imam's choice to impose kharaj while leaving inhabitants indicates that ownership remains with them. Kharaj is a tax on the land, not a transfer of ownership.
The ruling is based on public interest (maslahah) in maintaining agricultural production and revenue.
5
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that land conquered by force becomes state property (fay'). The Hanafis rely on the practice of the Caliphs, especially ʿUmar, as authoritative.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with strong evidence on both sides.

Source Text

قَالَ وَاَرْضُ السَّوَادِ مَمُلُوكَةٌ لِأهْلِهَا يَجُوزُبَيْعُهُمْ لَهَا وَتَصَرُّفُهُمْ فِيهَا لأَنَّ الْإِمَامَ إِذَا فَتَحَ أَرْضًا عُنُوَةً وَقَهُرَالَهُ أَنْ يُقِرَّ أَهْلَهَا عَلَيْهَا وَيَضَعَ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى رُوسِهِمُ الْحَرَاجَ فَتَبْقَى الْأَرَاضِي مَمْلُوكَةً لِّأَهْلِهَا وَقَدْ قَدَّمُنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ ترجمہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ سواد عراق کی زمین وہاں کے لوگوں کی مملوکہ ہے ۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کا اس زمین کو بیچنا اور اس میں تصرف کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ امام نے جب کسی زمین کو قہر اور طاقت سے فتح کیا تو اسے اختیار ہے کہ وہاں کے لوگوں کو اسی زمین پر باقی رکھے اور ان پر اور ان کی زمین پر خراج مقرر کرے اس طرح وہاں کی زمین وہاں کے باشندوں کی مملوک رہے گی ۔ اس مسئلہ کو ہم باب قسمتہ الغنائم میں پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
Ruling of the lands of Sawad Iraq. He said: The lands of Sawad are owned by their inhabitants; it is permissible for them to sell them and dispose of them, because when the imam conquers land by force and compulsion, he has the option to leave its inhabitants on it and impose kharaj on them and on their heads, so the lands remain owned by their inhabitants. We have presented this previously. Translation: Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said that the land of Sawad Iraq is owned by the people there, such that selling it and disposing of it is permissible for them. Because when the imam conquers a land by force and power, he has the option to keep the people on that land and impose kharaj on them and on their land; thus the land remains owned by its inhabitants. We have explained this earlier in the chapter on division of spoils.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Quduri: the lands of Sawad Iraq remain the property of their original inhabitants, and they are allowed to sell and transact in them. The proof is that the imam, when conquering land by force (ʿanwatan), has the choice to leave the inhabitants and impose kharaj on them and their land. This preserves their ownership. The commentary notes that this was already discussed in the chapter on division of spoils. The Hanafi position is clear: kharaj does not transfer ownership to the state; it is a tax on the land while ownership stays with the conquered people.

Key Terms
عنوة (ʿanwatan): By force and compulsion; conquest without a peace treaty, where the inhabitants submit after being overpowered.
خراج (kharāj): A land tax imposed on the conquered non-Muslim inhabitants who retain ownership and remain on their land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Conquered land by force with kharaj remains owned by its inhabitants, who may sell it.

Definition of Kharaji Land
Defining kharaji land and stating the Makkah exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define kharaji land, identify the two modes of acquisition (force and treaty), and explain the exception of Makkah.

Core Idea
Kharaji land is conquered land left with its inhabitants — kharaj is imposed, but Makkah is a unique exception.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi classification of conquered lands. Land taken by force or treaty where the original inhabitants remain becomes kharaji, meaning a land tax (kharaj) is levied on them. However, Makkah stands as a special case: conquered by force, yet no kharaj was imposed by the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this distinction is key to comprehending Hanafi land law and its basis in prophetic precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
The passage defines 'kharaji land' as land conquered by force (ʿanwa) where the inhabitants are left on it. Also includes land conquered by peace treaty (ṣulḥ) with the same result.
2
Locate the ruling and its reason
The author states that kharaj is imposed because the inhabitants are disbelievers and kharaj is more suitable for them. Note the talil (reasoning).
The term 'talil' refers to the causal reasoning behind the ruling.
3
Identify the exception
Makkah is excluded despite being conquered by force. The Prophet left its inhabitants without imposing kharaj. This makes Makkah 'ushri land, not kharaji.
This exception is specific to Makkah; no other territory shares this status.
4
Determine the practical implication
All conquered land where inhabitants remain is generally kharaji, but Makkah remains 'ushri due to the prophetic precedent. A mufti must know this distinction when classifying land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خراجی زمین کی تعریف
وَكُلُّ أَرْضِ فُتِحَتْ عَنْوَة فَأُقِرَّأَهلُهَا عَلَيْهَا فَهِيَ أَرْضُ خَرَاجِ وَكَذَا إِذَا صَالَحَهُمْ لِأَنَّ الْحَاجَةَ إِلَى ابْتِدَاءِ التَّرْظِيفِ عَلَى الْكَافِرِ وَالْخَرَاجُ أَلْيَقُ بِهِ وَمَكَةُ مَخصُوصٌ مِنْ هَذَا فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَتَحَهَا عَنْوَةً
وَتَرَكَهَا لِأَهْلِهَا وَلَمْ يُوْظِفِ الْخَرَاجَ
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بداری جلد بشتم

Definition of kharaji land. And every land conquered by force, and its inhabitants are left on it, is kharaji land; similarly if he made peace with them, because the need is to initially impose tax on the disbeliever, and kharaj is more suitable for him. Makkah is excluded from this, for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) conquered it by force and left it to its inhabitants and did not impose kharaj. Translation: And every land conquered by force... (to the end): Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary of Bidayah, volume 7: Translation: And every land conquered by force and compulsion, then its inhabitants are left there, that is kharaji land. Similarly, if peace was made with them, that land is also kharaji. Because the need to impose tax first arises upon the disbeliever, and kharaj is more suitable for him. Makkah is specially excluded from this. Thus the Messenger of Allah conquered Makkah by his force, left its inhabitants in place, and did not impose kharaj on them.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage defines kharaji land: land conquered by force (ʿanwatan) where the inhabitants remain on the land and kharaj is imposed. It also includes land conquered by peace treaty (ṣulḥan) because the inhabitants remain. The reasoning is that kharaj is more suitable for disbelievers. However, Makkah is an exception: although conquered by force, the Prophet left the inhabitants without imposing kharaj, making it 'ushri. The Hanafi position is that generally, conquered land left with its inhabitants becomes kharaji, but Makkah retains its special status.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A peace treaty with the conquered inhabitants, which also results in the land being kharaji as they remain with kharaj.
عَنْوَةً (ʿanwatan): By force, referring to conquest through military victory.
أَرْضِ خَرَاجِ (arḍ al-kharāj): Land subject to kharaj, a land tax imposed on non-Muslim owners of conquered lands.
مَخْصُوصٌ (makhṣūṣ): Excluded or specified, used here to indicate that Makkah is a special case exempt from the general rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it is located within the Arabian Peninsula

Key Takeaway
Kharaji land is defined by conquest (force or treaty) and the inhabitants' retention; Makkah is a unique exception due to prophetic practice.

Land Classification by Irrigation Source: Kharaji vs. 'Ushri
Ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir linking land type to water source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify conquered land as kharaji or 'ushri based on its irrigation source, citing the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir and explaining the underlying rationale (talil).

Core Idea
Water source determines tax status: river water makes conquered land kharaji; wells/springs make it 'ushri.

When Muslim armies conquer land by force, the default classification is 'kharaji' (land subject to kharaj tax). However, this passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir introduces a nuanced exception: the irrigation source matters. Land irrigated by rivers remains kharaji, but if irrigation relies on wells or springs dug by the occupants, it reverts to 'ushri (subject to 'ushr tax). The rationale is that 'ushr is linked to the land's natural produce, which depends on the water source. This lesson unpacks the conditions and proofs for this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its precondition
The act is the classification of conquered land. The precondition: the land must have been taken by force (عَنْوَةً).
Land conquered peacefully (sulhan) has its own rules.
2
Distinguish the two water sources
The passage specifies two types of irrigation: river water (مَاءُ الْأَنْهَارِ) and water extracted from wells or springs (عَيْن).
Rainwater is not mentioned here; it may be treated under a separate rule.
3
State the ruling for each source
If river water reaches the land → kharaji. If river water does not reach and a well/spring is used → 'ushri.
These are the two mutually exclusive outcomes.
4
Analyze the talil (rationale)
The passage explains: 'ushr is connected to the land's produce, and produce depends on water. Therefore, the classification follows the water source – whether it is 'ushri water (from wells/springs) or kharaji water (from rivers).
This is a causal link (ta'lil), showing the wisdom behind the distinction.
5
Identify the authority weight
The ruling is transmitted from al-Jami' al-Saghir, one of the six zahir al-riwayah works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. It carries high authority.
Zahir al-riwayah rulings are the primary basis for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہ زمین جو قہر اور طاقت سے حاصل کی گئی اور نہروں کے پانی سے سینچی گئی وہ خراجی ہے وَفِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ كُلُّ أَرْضِ فُتِحَتْ عَنْوَۃً فَوَصَلَ إِلَيْهَامَاءُ الْأَنْهَارِ فَهِيَ أَرْضُ خَرَاجِ وَمَالَمْ يَصِلُّ إِلَيْهَامَاءُ الْأَنْهَارِ وَ اسْتَخْرِجَ مِنْهَا عَيْنَ فَهِيَ أَرْضُ عُشْرِ لِأَنَّ الْعُشْرَ يَتَعَلَّمُ بِالْأَرْضِ النَّاتِيَةِ وَنَمَاؤُهَا بِمَائِهَا فَيُعْتَبَرُ السَّفْى بِمَاءِ الْعُشْرِ أَوْ بِمَاءِ الْخَرَاجِ
ترجمہ و فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِير .. الخ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جو زمین قہر اور طاقت سے فتح کی گئی ہو پھر اس زمین میں نہروں کا پانی پہنچا تو وہ زمین خراجی ہے اور جس میں نہروں کا پانی نہیں پہنچا بلکہ وہیں کوئی چشمہ یا کنواں نکالا گیا تو وہ زمین عشری ہے۔ کیونکہ عشری کا تعلق زمین کی پیداوار سے ہوتا ہے اور اس کی پیداوار پانی سے ہوتی ہے لہذا اعتبار عشری پانی یا خراجی پانی سے سیراب کرنے پر موقوف ہو گا۔ یعنی جیسے پانی سے اس کی سیرابی ہوگی اس کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔
That land which is obtained by force and power and irrigated by the water of rivers is kharaji. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Every land conquered by force, and the water of rivers reaches it, is kharaji land; but if river water does not reach it, and instead a spring or well is extracted from it, then it is 'ushri land, because 'ushr is connected to the producing land, and its growth is by its water; so consideration depends on irrigation by 'ushri water or kharaji water. Translation: And in al-Jami' al-Saghir... etc.: And in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is that any land conquered by force and power, then if river water reaches that land, it is kharaji; and if river water does not reach it, but rather a spring or well is dug there, then it is 'ushri land, because 'ushr is connected to the produce of the land, and its produce is by water; therefore the ruling depends on whether it is irrigated by 'ushri water or kharaji water.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir provides a secondary rule for classifying conquered land based on its water source. Even if conquered by force, if the land is irrigated by rivers (which are often state-managed or large-scale), it is kharaji. If it is irrigated by privately developed wells or springs, it is 'ushri. The reason given is that 'ushr is tied to the land's produce, and the water source determines the ease of cultivation. Thus, land irrigated by river water (which may imply more productive or larger areas) becomes kharaji, while land irrigated by wells (more limited, perhaps requiring effort) remains 'ushri. This is a technical distinction within Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
عيون (ʿuyūn): Springs or wells from which water is extracted for irrigation, as opposed to river water.
خراج (kharāj): A land tax imposed on conquered lands that remain in the hands of non-Muslims or are public property.
عشر (ʿushr): Tithe on agricultural produce, typically 10% on rain-irrigated land and 5% on labor-irrigated land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Jami' al-Saghir, land conquered by force is 'ushri if it is irrigated by what?
A) Rivers
B) Rain
C) Wells or springs
D) Canals

Key Takeaway
The irrigation source (river vs. well/spring) determines whether conquered land is classified as kharaji or 'ushri in Hanafi fiqh.

6 min
Abu Yusuf's Rule for Classifying Revived Dead Land
Abu Yusuf's rule and the Basra exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Yusuf's principle that revived dead land takes the tax classification ('ushri or kharaji) of the nearest inhabited land, and identify the exception for Basra based on ijma.

Core Idea
A revived dead land follows the ruling of its nearest inhabited area — unless consensus overrides qiyas.

In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of revived dead land as 'ushri or kharaji is not arbitrary. Imam Abu Yusuf established a clear rule: the land's location (hayyiz) determines its status. This lesson unpacks his reasoning, the analogy to the courtyard (fina') of a house, and the notable exception of Basra where the Companions' consensus overturned the qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Yusuf's position
Identify the ruling: revived dead land is classified according to the nearest inhabited land — if near kharaji land, it is kharaji; if near 'ushri land, it is 'ushri.
2
Understand the qiyas khafi
The analogy: just as the courtyard (fina') of a house takes the ruling of the house, the area (hayyiz) of dead land takes the ruling of adjacent inhabited land.
This is a qiyas deriving the ruling from the fina' principle.
3
Identify the Basra exception
Basra is in the area of kharaji land, yet it is unanimously considered 'ushri due to the Companions' ijma, which overrides qiyas.
This is an example of istihsan based on ijma.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a location (e.g., near Kufa which is 'ushri), classify a revived dead land as 'ushri; near a kharaji village as kharaji.
The practical result determines zakat or kharaj liability.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf's view is one among the Hanafi imams; others may consider the reviver's intention or the land's original status.
The text presents Abu Yusuf's opinion without mention of disagreement, implying it is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ارض موات کب خراجی ہوتی ہے
قَالَ وَمَنْ احْيا أَرْضًا مَوَاتًا فَهِيَ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ مُعْتَبَرَةُ بِخَيْرِهَا فَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ حَيْزِ أَرْضِ الْخَرَاجِ وَمَعْنَاهُ بِقَرُبِهِ فَهِيَ خَرَاحِيَّةُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ خَيْرِ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِفَهِيَ عُشْرِيَّةُ وَالْبَصْرَةُ . يَة وَالبَصْرَة عِندَهُ كُلُّها عُشْرِيَّةِ بِإِجْمَاعَ الصَّحَابَةِ لِأَنَّ خَيْرَ الشَّئُ يُعْطَى لَهُ حُكْمُهُ كَفَنَاءِ الدَّارِ يُعْطَى لَهُ حُكْمُ الدَّارِ حَتَّى يَجُوزُ لِصَاحِبِهَا الْاِنْتِفَاعُ بِهِ وَكَذَا لَا يَجُورُ أَحَدٌ مَاقَرُبَ مِنَ الْعَامِرِ وَكَانَ الْقِيَاسُ فِى الْبَصْرَةِ أَنْ تَكُونَ خَرَاحِيَّةً لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ حَيْزُ أَرْضِ الْخَرَاجِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ وَظَفُوا عَلَيْهَا الْعُشْرَ فَتَرِكَ الْقِيَاسُ لِإِجْمَاعِهِمْ
ترجمہ اور جس نے کسی مردہ زمین کو زندہ کیا ۔ یعنی جنگل کی غیر مزروعہ زمین (غیر آباد ) کو مزروعہ ( آباد ) کیا تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس کا محل وقوع ( کہ کیسی جگہ میں ہے) دیکھا جائے گا۔ کہ اگر وہ زمین خرابی زمین کے قریب ہو تو وہ زمین بھی خراجی زمین ہوگی اور اگر عشری زمین کے قریب ہو تو وہ بھی عشری زمین ہوگی۔ اور ابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بصرہ کی زمین سب عشری ہے کیونکہ صحابہ کرام کا اس پر اجماع ہے ۔ رواہ ابن عبد البر ۔ کیونکہ جو پیر جس موقع پر ہو اسی کا حکم پاتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ فناء دار کو اس دار کا حکم دیا جاتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس دار کے مالک کو فناء دار سے فائدہ اٹھانے کی پوری اجازت ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح آبادی کے قریب جو زمین ہوتی ہے اس کو لینا جائز نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بصرہ کے بارے میں ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ وہ بھی خراجی ہو کیونکہ وہ
When does dead land become kharaji? He said: Whoever revives dead land, in the view of Abu Yusuf, it is considered by its area; if it is from the area of kharaji land, meaning by its proximity, then it is kharaji; if it is from the area of 'ushri land, then it is 'ushri. And Basra, in his view, is all 'ushri by consensus of the Companions because the area of a thing gives its ruling, like the courtyard of a house gives the ruling of the house, such that its owner is allowed to benefit from it; similarly, no one may seize what is near the inhabited area. And the qiyas for Basra is that it should be kharaji because it is from the area of kharaji land, but the Companions imposed 'ushr on it, so the qiyas was abandoned due to their consensus. Translation: And whoever revives dead land, i.e., uncultivated forest land (uninhabited) to cultivated (inhabited), then according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), its location (what kind of place it is) will be considered: if that land is near kharaji land, then it will also be kharaji; if it is near 'ushri land, it will be 'ushri. And according to Abu Yusuf, the land of Basra is all 'ushri because the Companions have consensus on it, narrated by Ibn Abd al-Barr. Because the area takes the ruling of its location, just as the courtyard of a house takes the ruling of the house, so the owner of the house has full permission to benefit from the courtyard. Similarly, land near inhabited area cannot be taken. Regarding Basra, according to Abu Yusuf, the qiyas demanded that it be kharaji because it is from the area of kharaji land, but the Companions imposed 'ushr on it, so the qiyas was abandoned due to their consensus.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on reviving dead (uninhabited) land according to Imam Abu Yusuf. He says that such land takes the classification of the nearest inhabited land: if it is near kharaji land, it becomes kharaji; if near 'ushri land, it becomes 'ushri. This is based on the principle that an area (hayyiz) takes the ruling of its adjacent inhabited land, similar to how a courtyard (fina') takes the ruling of the attached house. The passage then gives the exception of Basra: although by qiyas (analogy) Basra should be kharaji because it is in the area of kharaji land, the Companions unanimously agreed that it is 'ushri, so that consensus overrides the qiyas. This is an example of istihsan based on ijma. The commentary also notes that the prohibition of seizing land near inhabited areas is related to this principle.

Key Terms
موات (mawāt): Dead land, uninhabited and uncultivated land not owned by anyone, which can be revived by bringing it under cultivation.
حیز (ḥayyiz): The area or district to which land belongs; used to determine whether land is 'ushri or kharaji based on proximity.
فناء (fināʾ): Courtyard or open space attached to a house, which takes the same legal ruling as the house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what determines whether revived dead land is 'ushri or kharaji?
A) The intention of the reviver
B) The type of crops grown
C) The proximity to 'ushri or kharaji land
D) The method of irrigation

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's rule: the hayyiz of the nearest inhabited land determines whether revived dead land is 'ushri or kharaji, except where consensus (ijma) overrides qiyas, as in Basra.

Kharaj Not Cancelled by Abandoning Cultivation
Ruling on kharaj obligation when land is left uncultivated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that kharaj remains obligatory when land is left uncultivated and explain the basis in qiyas, and identify the restriction on the subsidiary ruling about switching to a lesser crop.

Core Idea
Kharaj remains due because the owner had the ability to cultivate; abandonment does not cancel the obligation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: a landowner leaves his kharaj land uncultivated. Does the tax disappear? The ruling is clear: kharaj is still due. The reasoning goes to the heart of Hanafi legal theory — obligation is tied to ability, not actual use. The commentary adds a subsidiary point about switching crops, but with a crucial caution: it is not to be given as a fatwa, to protect people from oppressive rulers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn states: if the owner abandons the land (does not cultivate), the kharaj is still upon him. So the ruling is wajib (obligatory payment).
The act here is leaving land uncultivated; the ruling is that the financial obligation remains.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is given as: 'because the ability (tamakkun) was established and he is the one who wasted it.' This is a qiyas: the owner had full ability to cultivate, so the obligation based on that ability is not removed by his choice to waste it.
This is a reasoning (ta'lil) based on the concept of tamakkun.
3
Understand the Subsidiary Ruling
The commentators (mashayikh) add: if the owner switches from a high-value crop (e.g., saffron) to a low-value one (e.g., millet) without excuse, he must pay the higher kharaj because he deliberately wasted the potential increase.
This is an extension of the same logic: waste of potential incurs the higher obligation.
4
Note the Fatwa Restriction
The text says: 'this is known and not given as a fatwa, so that oppressors do not dare to take people's wealth.' The ruling is theoretically sound but withheld from fatwa to prevent abuse by unjust rulers.
This reflects Hanafi concern for public welfare (maslaha) and protection from tyranny.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Concern
The restriction shows that fiqh rulings are sometimes withheld in practice if they would lead to greater harm. The school prioritizes preventing oppression over applying the strict letter of the law in this case.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) for the sake of maslaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مالک زمین نے اسے بے کار چھوڑ دیا تو خراج ساقط نہ ہوگا
قَالَ وَإِنْ عَطَّلَهَا صَاحِبُهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ لِأَنَّ التَّمَكُنَ كَانَ ثَابِما وَهُوَ الَّذِى فَوَّتَهُ قَالُوا مَنِ انتَقَلَ إِلَى أَخَسِ الْأَمْرَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ الْأَعْلَى لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الَّذِى ضَيَّعَ الرِّيَادَةَ وَهُدَايُعْرَفُ وَلَا يُفْتَى بِهِ كَيْلَا يَتَجَرَّءَ الظَّلَمَةُ عَلَى أَحْدِ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ
ترجمه قَالَ وَإِنْ عَطَّلَها ... الخ اور اگر مالک زمین نے کھیتی کو یوں ہی بے کار چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر خراج لازم آ جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اسے کھیتی کرنے کی پوری قدرت موجود تھی پھر بھی اس نے جان بوجھ کر وہ ضائع کر دیا۔ مشائخ رحمۃ اللہ علیہم نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی زمین میں قیمتی چیز مثلاً زعفران وغیرہ پیدا ہوتی ہو پھر بھی مالک نے کسی عذر کے بغیر معمولی سی چیز مثلاً جوار وغیرہ کی کھیتی کر لی تو اس پر اعلی چیز کا ہی حسب سابق لگان لگایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے قصدا اعلی مقدار ضائع کر دی ہے۔ مگر یہ بات صرف معلوم ہونی چاہئے ۔ اور اس کا فتوی نہیں دینا چاہئے تا کہ ظالم حکام رعایا کے مال میں جرات نہ کریں۔
If the owner abandons it, then upon him is the kharaj, because the ability was established and he is the one who wasted it. They said: whoever moves to a lesser of the two things without excuse, then upon him is the higher kharaj, because he is the one who wasted the increase. And this is known and not given as fatwa, so that oppressors do not dare to take people's wealth. Translation: ... (Urdu explanation)
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on kharaj. The matn of al-Hidayah declares that if a landowner leaves his land uncultivated, he is still liable for kharaj because he had the ability to cultivate and wasted it. The commentary adds a subsidiary ruling from the mashayikh: if a landowner switches from a high-value crop (like saffron) to a low-value one (like millet) without excuse, he must pay kharaj on the higher crop since he intentionally wasted its potential. However, this opinion is to be known but not issued as a fatwa to prevent unjust rulers from exploiting it. This reflects the Hanafi concern for public welfare (maslaha) and protecting subjects from oppression.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): A land tax imposed on conquered lands that remain in non-Muslim hands or are treated as kharaj lands.
تَمَكُّن (tamakkun): Ability or capacity; in this context, the owner's capacity to cultivate the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Kharaj is halved.
D) Kharaj is deferred until he cultivates.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is tied to the ability to cultivate, not actual cultivation; thus, abandonment does not cancel the obligation, but the subsidiary ruling on crop switching is withheld from fatwa to prevent oppression.

Kharaj collected from a new Muslim convert
Ruling that kharaj remains after conversion to Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj after conversion and explain the legal reasoning (talil) using the concept of mu'nah.

Core Idea
Kharaj remains on converted Muslims because it is tied to the land's capacity, not the owner's religion.

In this passage, we encounter a key distinction in Islamic fiscal law: the continuity of land tax (kharaj) after a landowner embraces Islam. While 'ushr (tithe) is based on the cultivator's faith, kharaj is attached to the land itself. The author explains why the obligation persists, using the term 'mu'nah' (expenditure) as the effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a person from ahl al-kharaj (non-Muslims subject to kharaj) converting to Islam. The ruling: kharaj is still taken from him as before.
The ruling is clear: no change in obligation.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the statement: 'because in it (kharaj) is the meaning of mu'nah (expenditure)'. This indicates that the tax is considered an ongoing expenditure on the land.
Mu'nah is a continuous attribute.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (relevance of the proof)
Mu'nah is attached to the land itself, not to the person's religious status. Therefore, the obligation remains even after conversion. The text says: 'so it is considered expenditure in the state of continuity, so it is possible to keep it upon the Muslim.'
Contrast with 'ushr, which is based on the cultivator's faith and would be cancelled upon conversion.
4
Note the distinction from other taxes
Unlike 'ushr, which is a religious tithe, kharaj is a land-based tax. Thus, conversion does not alter the land's classification.
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiscal law.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
There is no known Hanafi ikhtilaf on this ruling; it is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) and mufta bihi.
The text itself states the position as definitive.

Source Text

اہل خراج میں سے جو مسلمان ہو گیا اس سے خراج لیا جائے گا
وَمَنْ أَسْلَمَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرَاحِ أُخِذَمِنَهُ الْحَرَاجِ عَلَى حَالِهِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْمُؤْنَةِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ مَؤُنَةٌ فِي حَالَةِ الْبَقَاءِ فَأَمْكَنَ إبْقَاؤُهُ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ
ترجمہ اور جن لوگوں پر خراج واجب ہوا گر ان میں سے کوئی مسلمان ہو گیا تو اس سے بدستور سابق خراج لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ خراج کے معنی ( محصول اور لگان کے علاوہ ) اخراجات اور خرچ کے بھی ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے بعد میں یعنی حالت بقاء میں بھی اس میں خراج اور مونت ہی کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کسی مسلمان پر اس حالت کو باقی رکھنا ممکن ہے ( یعنی مسلمان پر ابتداء تو خراج لازم نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے مگر خراجی زمین ہو جانے کے بعد اس کو خراجی کہنا ممکن ہو جائے گا )۔
And whoever becomes Muslim from the people of kharaj, kharaj is taken from him as before, because in it is the meaning of expenditure (mu'nah), so it is considered expenditure in the state of continuity, so it is possible to keep it upon the Muslim. Translation: ... (Urdu explanation)
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage rules that a person from ahl al-kharaj (non-Muslims liable for kharaj) who embraces Islam continues to pay kharaj. The reason is that kharaj has the meaning of mu'nah (expenditure/tax), and this aspect remains after conversion. It is not like 'ushr which is based on religion. Initially, a Muslim cannot be subjected to kharaj ab initio, but once the land is already classified as kharaj land, the obligation continues even after the owner becomes Muslim. This distinguishes between the imposition and the continuity of the tax.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax on conquered territory, treated as a continuous expenditure on the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Kharaj is still taken from him as before.
C) Kharaj is replaced by 'ushr.
D) Kharaj is reduced by half.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a land-based tax that persists even after the owner embraces Islam, because its effective cause (mu'nah) is continuous.

No 'Ushr on Kharaj Land: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Combining Land Taxes
Inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i on combining 'ushr and kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on combining 'ushr and kharaj and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the three Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
'Ushr and kharaj cannot combine on the same land because they arise from mutually exclusive causes: voluntary Islam vs. conquest by force.

This lesson addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the imposition of land taxes. At issue is whether 'ushr (tithe on produce) and kharaj (land tax on conquered territories) can be levied together on the same land. The Hanafi school firmly holds that they are mutually exclusive, while Shafi'is argue they are distinct obligations. Understanding this dispute clarifies the principles of Islamic land taxation and the methodology of legal proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
State the Hanafi position: No 'ushr is due on the produce of kharaj land; only kharaj is payable.
2
State the Shafi'i Position and Rationale
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that both taxes can be combined because they are different rights with different causes: kharaj on the landowner for the land's capacity, and 'ushr on the actual produce.
3
Examine the Hadith Proof
The Hanafis cite the hadith: 'No 'ushr and kharaj combine in a Muslim’s land.' Note its chain is weak but supported by other evidence.
4
Examine the Historical Consensus Proof
All Muslim rulers, just or unjust, have never combined 'ushr and kharaj. This consistent practice constitutes a strong proof (ijma' amali).
5
Examine the Rational Proof
Kharaj applies to land conquered by force; 'ushr applies to land whose people accepted Islam voluntarily. These two descriptions cannot coexist in one land, so only one tax applies.
6
Note the Practical Consequence (Thamarah) and Zakat
The dispute affects zakat al-tijarah on land bought for trade: Hanafis say no zakat, only the land's tax. Shafi'is would impose both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خراجی زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر نہیں
وَلَا عُشْرَ فِي الْخَارِجِ مِنْ أَرْضِ الْحَرَاجِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُمَا حَقَّانِ مُخْتَلِفَانِ وَجَبَافِي مَحَلَّيْنِ بِسَبَبَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ فَلَايَتَنَا فَيَانِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يَجْتَمِعُ عُشُرٍّ وَخَرَاجٌ فِي أَرْضِ مُسْلِمِ وَلأَنَّ أَحَدًا مِّنْ أئِمَّةِ العَدْلِ وَالجَوْرِ لَمْ يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا وَكَفَى بِإِجْمَاعِهِمْ حُجَّةً وَلاَنَّ الْخَرَاجَ يَجِبُ فِى أَرْضِ فُتِحَتُ عَنوَةً وقهر او العُشْرُ فِي أَرْضِ أَسْلَمَ أَهْلُهَا طَوْعًا وَالْوَصْفَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي أَرْضِ وَاحِدَةٍ وَسَبَبُ الْحَقَّيْنِ وَاحِدُوَهُوَ الْأَرْضُ النَّامِيةُ إِلا أَنه يُعْتَبَرُ فِى الْعُشْرِ تَحْقِيقا وفِي الْخَرَاجِ تَقْدِيرًا وَلِهَدَايُضَا فَانِ إِلَى الْأَرْضِ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ الزَّكوةُ مَعَ أُحَدِهِمَا
ترجمہ وَلَا عُشْرَ فِي الْخَارِج الخ اور خراجی زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس میں فقط خراج لازم آئے گا۔ اور شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس میں سے عشر اور خراج دونوں لئے جائیں گے ۔ کیونکہ یہ دو مختلف حقوق ہیں جو دو موقعوں میں دو مختلف سبب سے واجب ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ان کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے (کہ ایک کے ہونے سے دوسرا نہ ہو ) کیونکہ خراج تو مالک کے ذمہ زمین کی قوت پیدائش کے سبب سے ہے اور عشر پیداوار پرحقیقی پیدائش کے سبب سے ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسلمان کی زمین میں عشر و خراج دونوں جمع نہیں ہوں گے۔ ابن عدی نے ضعیف سند سے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمانوں کے اماموں میں سے وہ خواہ ظالم ہو یا عادل ہو کسی نے بھی عشر و خراج کو جمع نہیں کیا ہے۔ اس طرح ان کا متفقہ عمل بھی ایک دلیل ہوئی اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ خراج تو ایسی زمین میں واجب ہوتا ہے جو تلوار کے زور سے قہر افتح کی گئی ہو ۔ اور عشر ایسی زمین میں واجب ہوتا ہے جہاں کے لوگ اپنی خوشی سے مسلمان ہوئے ہوں اور یہ دونوں باتیں ایک ہی زمین میں ایک ساتھ نہیں پائی جاسکتی ہیں ۔ (اسی لئے صحابہ کرام سے بھی دونوں کو جمع کرنا منقول نہیں ہے ) اور عشر و خراج دونوں کا سبب ایک ہے یعنی پیداوار والی زمین ہے البتہ ان میں صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ عشر میں حقیقی اور یقینی پیداوار کا اعتبار ہے اور خراج میں تقدیری پیداوار یعنی زراعت پر صرف قادر ہونا ہی کافی ہے لیکن حقیقتہ زمین ہی سبب ہے۔ اسی لئے دونوں کی نسبت زمین کی طرف ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے بولتے ہیں کہ عشر زمین یا خراج زمین اور ایسا ہی اختلاف زکوۃ کے ساتھ عشر یا خراج جمع کرنے میں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر عشری یا خراجی زمین تجارت کی نیت سے کسی نے خریدی تو ہمارے نزدیک اس میں تجارت کی زکوۃ نہیں ہوگی بلکہ صرف عشری زمین ہونے سے عشرور نہ خراج لازم آئے گا۔ تشریح حاصل یہ کہ ابن عدی کی مثل دیگر روایات میں بھی رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ فرمان منقول ہے کہ مسلمان کی زمین پر عشر وخراج (ایک ساتھ ) جمع نہیں ہو سکتے۔ لہذا صرف بیجی ابن عنبہ پر جرح کی وجہ سے متذکرہ روایت کو باطل قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا۔ لہذا احناف کے مؤقفہ عشر وخراج جمع نہیں ہوں گے ) کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے متن ہدایہ کی مستدلہ روایت لَا يَجْتَمِعُ عُشُرُ وَ حَرَاجٌ فِي أَرْضِ مُسْلِمٍ قابل حجت کا عشر وخراج دونوں کو جمع کر کے وصول نہ کرنا اس بنا پر تھا کہ حق و انصاف کا تقاضا یہی ہے کہ عشر و خراج کو جمع نہ کیا جائے ۔ لیکن ظالم حکمرانوں کا ہر دو عشر وخراج) کو جمع نہ کرنا یا تو شرعی نکتہ نگاہ کے پیش نظر علماء کے فتاوی کی بنا پر تھا کیونکہ ظالم حکمرانوں کا جبر و تشد د عموما سیاسی اختلاف کی بنیاد پر ہوتا ہے۔ اس کے پس منظر میں صرف اقتدار پر قابض رہنے کی تدابیر ہوا کرتی ہیں۔ نظریاتی میدان ( نظریہ اسلام) میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور عشر و خراج لاگو کرنے کا مسئلہ خالص شرعی ہے۔ اسلئے مسلمان ظالم حاکم ہونے کے باوجود اپنے اندر کچھ نہ کچھ ایمان اور شعائر اسلام کے احترام کی رمق
And there is no 'ushr on the produce from kharaj land. al-Shafi'i said: combine between them because they are two different rights that become obligatory in two places due to two different causes, so there is no contradiction. And our proof is the saying of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam): 'No 'ushr and kharaj combine in a Muslim's land.' And because not one of the rulers, just or unjust, combined between them, and their consensus is sufficient as proof. And because kharaj is obligatory on land conquered by force and overpowering, and 'ushr is on land whose people became Muslims voluntarily, and the two descriptions cannot combine in one land. And the cause of both rights is one, and it is the productive land, except that in 'ushr actual (production) is considered, and in kharaj estimated (potential) is considered. And because of this they are attributed to the land. And upon this disagreement is zakat with either of them. Translation: ... (Urdu explanation)
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether 'ushr and kharaj can be imposed together on the same land. The Hanafi position, stated first, is that there is no 'ushr on the produce of kharaj land; only kharaj is due. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that both can be combined because they are distinct rights: kharaj is on the landowner's liability for the land's productive capacity, while 'ushr is on the actual produce. The Hanafi response provides three proofs: (1) A hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) states that 'ushr and kharaj do not combine in a Muslim's land. The commentary notes that this hadith is narrated by Ibn 'Adi with a weak chain, but it is supported by other evidences. (2) Historical consensus (al-Ijma' al-'Amali): All Muslim rulers, both just and unjust, have never combined 'ushr and kharaj, and their consistent practice constitutes a strong proof. (3) Rational proof: Kharaj applies to land conquered by force (anwatan), while 'ushr applies to land whose people accepted Islam voluntarily. These two descriptions cannot coexist in the same land, so only one tax applies. Additionally, the cause (sabab) of both is the productive land, but 'ushr considers actual produce while kharaj considers estimated potential, and since each is attributed to the land, they cannot be combined. The passage also notes that the same dispute applies to zakat with either 'ushr or kharaj: if someone buys 'ushri or kharaji land with the intention of trade, no zakat al-tijarah is due; only the land's applicable tax ('ushr or kharaj) applies. The commentary elaborates on the hadith's chain and the reasoning of rulers, emphasizing that even unjust rulers did not combine them, showing the strength of the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
عشر (ʻushr): A tithe (10% or 5%) on produce of Muslim-owned agricultural land.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax on conquered territories, considered an expenditure on the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary hadith proof cited by the Hanafis to support their position that 'ushr and kharaj cannot combine?
A) 'No 'ushr and kharaj combine in a Muslim's land.'
B) 'The land of Muslims is subject to 'ushr.'
C) 'Kharaj is due on every land.'
D) 'Combine 'ushr and kharaj for justice.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that 'ushr and kharaj are mutually exclusive because their causes (conquest by force vs. voluntary submission) cannot coexist in the same land, supported by hadith, historical consensus, and rational proof.

12 min
Why 'Ushr and Kharaj Cannot Combine on Muslim Land
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and rebuttals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that 'ushr and kharaj cannot combine on a single Muslim-owned land and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
'Ushr and kharaj share the same cause—productive land—so they cannot be imposed together.

Land taxation in Islamic law distinguishes between 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax), each tied to the land's origin. But what happens when a single piece of land could theoretically attract both? The Hanafi school firmly rejects any combination, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues they are separate rights. This lesson unpacks the proofs and reveals why the Hanafi position prevails.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the opening line: only one tax applies, either 'ushr or kharaj, never both.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds both can be collected because they arise from different causes.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues: kharaj is on the landowner for capacity, 'ushr on the produce—so no contradiction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis counter with three proofs: hadith, consensus of rulers, and mutual exclusivity of the land's descriptions.
The hadith 'لا يجتمع عشر وخراج في أرض مسلم' is cited despite its weak chain, supported by historical practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice: a Hanafi farmer pays only one tax; a Shafi'i farmer would pay both.

نکتہ نگاہ کے پیش نظر علماء کے فتاوی کی بنا پر تھا کیونکہ ظالم حکمرانوں کا جبر و تشدد عموما سیاسی اختلاف کی بنیاد پر ہوتا ہے۔ اس کے پس منظر میں صرف اقتدار پر قابض رہنے کی تدابیر ہوا کرتی ہیں۔ نظریاتی میدان ( نظریہ اسلام) میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور عشر و خراج لاگو کرنے کا مسئلہ خالص شرعی ہے۔ اسلئے مسلمان ظالم حاکم ہونے کے باوجود اپنے اندر کچھ نہ کچھ ایمان اور شعائر اسلام کے احترام کی رمق ضرور رکھتا ہے۔ اسلئے مملکت اسلامیہ کے ظالم حکمران بھی عشر و خراج کو جمع نہیں کرتے تھے۔ چنانچہ اس صورت میں عادل و ظالم حکمران کا متفقہ فیصلہ ( عشر و خراج کا جمع نہ ہونا ) قابل حجت ہے۔ عشر کا تعلق نفس زمین کے ساتھ ہے پیداوار ضروری نہیں ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مسلمان سے ہر پیداوار پر عشر وصول کیا جاتا ہے بخلاف خراج کے کہ اس کا تعلق محض پیداوار کے ساتھ ہے اگر پیداوار موجود ہے تو خراج ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ اسی امر کو ہدایہ کے متن میں واضح کیا گیا ہے کہ عشر میں تحقیقی پیداوار معتبر ہے اور خراج میں تقدیری پیداوار کا اعتبار ہے۔ جو زمین قہر و غلبہ سے حاصل کی جائے اس پر خراج لاگو ہوتا ہے اور جس زمین کا مالک مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر عشر واجب ہوتا ہے ایک ہی زمین میں یہ دونوں وصف جمع نہیں ہو سکتے ۔
اس توجیہ میں صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کے استدلال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ ان کا استدلال یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں حق مختلف ہیں ۔ اور یہ دو محل میں مختلف سبب سے واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا عشر و خراج کا جمع ہونا منافی نہیں۔ امام شافعی کے اس استدلال کے جواب میں کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ دونوں وصف ایک جگہ جمع نہیں ہو سکتے اور ان دونوں کا سبب مختلف نہیں بلکہ ایک ہے اور وہ پیداوار والی زمین کا وجود ہے لہذا عشر و خراج جمع کرنے کے منافی ہونے کا تحقق ہو گیا۔ اختلاف زکوۃ کے حوالے سے بھی احناف کا موقف قوی ہے۔ کیونکہ جس عشری یا خراجی زمین کو تجارت کی نیت سے خریدا جاتا ہے اس پر تجارت پر مبنی زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اگر وہ (زمین ) تجارت کی نیت سے نہ خریدی جائے تو اس پر زکوۃ تجارت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف عشر و خراج کے کہ زمین کے عشری ہونے پر عشر واجب ہوتا ہے اور خراجی ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر خراج عائد ہوتا ہے خواہ اسے (زمین کو ) مزارعت و مشارکت ، مستاجری کی نیت سے خریدا جائے۔ کیونکہ عشر وخراج وجوبی وظیفہ ہیں جو زمین کی موجودگی میں کسی بھی صورت میں مالک سے ساقط نہیں ہوتے جبکہ تجارت کی نیت سے زمین نہ خریدنے کی صورت میں زکوۃ تجارت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا اختلاف زکوۃ کے حوالے سے بھی امام شافعی کا قول محل نظر ہے۔ چنانچہ اس پوری بحث سے باور ہوا که امام ابو حنیفہ و احناف کا قول رائج ہے اور امام شافعی کا موقف مرجوح متصور ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And no tithe is due on the produce of kharaj land, meaning only kharaj is obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i said that both 'ushr and kharaj should be taken from it, because these are two different rights that become obligatory on two occasions by two different causes, so there is no contradiction between them (that the existence of one prevents the other), because kharaj is on the landowner due to the land's productive capacity, while 'ushr is on the produce due to actual production. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Ushr and kharaj do not combine on a Muslim's land.' Ibn 'Adi narrated it with a weak chain. A second proof is that none of the Imams of the Muslims, whether just or unjust, have combined both; their consensus is sufficient as evidence. And also because kharaj becomes obligatory on land conquered by force, while 'ushr is on land whose people embraced Islam voluntarily, and these two descriptions do not meet in one land. The cause of both rights is one, namely the productive land, except that 'ushr considers actual production while kharaj considers estimated production, and therefore both are attributed to the land. Likewise, the difference regarding zakat combined with one of them. So if a person buys 'ushri or kharaji land with the intention of trade, according to us no zakat of trade is due on it, only 'ushr or kharaj as per the land type. Summary: The hadith 'Ushr and kharaj do not combine on a Muslim's land' is admissible evidence despite criticism of its chain. The second proof from the consensus of just and unjust rulers also suffices. The discussion refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that the two rights are different and due on different causes; instead, both have the same cause—the land's productivity. Regarding zakat, Hanafi view is strong: if land is not bought for trade, no zakat of trade is due, unlike 'ushr and kharaj which are obligatory dues that do not fall off under any circumstance. Thus the Hanafi position is the operative one. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the combination of 'ushr (tithes) and kharaj (land tax) on a single Muslim-owned land. The text begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: no 'ushr is due on the produce of kharaj land; only kharaj applies. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that both should be collected because they are distinct rights from different causes: kharaj is on the landowner for the land's productive capacity, and 'ushr is on the actual produce. The Hanafi response, as presented in Al-Hidayah, provides multiple proofs. First, a hadith directly states that 'ushr and kharaj do not combine on a Muslim's land. Despite its chain being considered weak by Ibn 'Adi, the author of Hidayah argues it remains admissible due to other supportive narrations. Second, there is consensus (ijma) of all Muslim rulers, both just and unjust, as none have ever collected both simultaneously, which serves as a strong historical practice. Third, rational proof: kharaj applies to land conquered by force, and 'ushr to land whose owners converted peacefully—these two descriptions cannot coexist in one land. The commentator explains that both taxes share the same cause, which is the productive land itself, though 'ushr considers actual produce and kharaj considers estimated capacity. The discussion extends to zakat: if 'ushri or kharaji land is purchased for trade, the Hanafi view is that no zakat of trade is due; only the land's inherent tax applies. The passage concludes that the Hanafi position is the relied-upone (rajih) and Imam al-Shafi'i's view is considered preponderated (marjuh).

Key Terms
الْعُشْر (al-'ushr): The tithe (one-tenth) on agricultural produce from land whose owners embraced Islam peacefully, considered worship-related (zakawi).
الْخَرَاج (al-kharaj): Land tax imposed on land conquered by force, assessed on estimated productive capacity, not actual yield.
الْوَصْفَانِ (al-wasfān): The two descriptions: land conquered by force (for kharaj) and land whose people embraced voluntarily (for 'ushr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on combining 'ushr and kharaj on a single Muslim-owned land?
A) Both must be paid because they are separate rights.
B) Only one applies, either 'ushr or kharaj, depending on the land's origin.
C) Neither applies because the land is Muslim-owned.
D) The landowner may choose which to pay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school firmly rules that 'ushr and kharaj cannot combine on Muslim land because they share the same cause—the productive land itself—and historical consensus supports this.

Kharaj Not Repeated with Repeated Harvests in a Year
Ruling statement with brief proof from practice of 'Umar (ra).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the repetition of kharaj with multiple harvests and distinguish it from 'ushr, citing the proof from the practice of 'Umar (ra).

Core Idea
Kharaj is a single annual levy, not multiplied by multiple harvests, unlike 'ushr which is per harvest.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from Kitab al-Siyar that clarifies a common point of confusion: how is kharaj (land tax) affected when a piece of land produces multiple harvests in a single year? The passage provides a clear answer with a brief proof from Caliph 'Umar's practice and contrasts it with the treatment of 'ushr (tithe).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the levying of kharaj on land. The ruling stated is that kharaj is not repeated when harvests are repeated within a year. It is a single annual obligation (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the action of Caliph 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (ra), who did not fix kharaj as a repeated levy. In Hanafi usul, the practice of a companion (especially a caliph) is a valid source of law.
3
Contrast with 'ushr
The passage explicitly contrasts kharaj with 'ushr. 'Ushr is a proportional share of actual produce and thus applies to every harvest. Kharaj is a fixed estimated tax and does not vary with the number of harvests.
This contrast highlights the different legal natures: kharaj is taqdiri (estimated), 'ushr is haqiqi (actual).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَتَكَرَّرُ الْخَرَاجُ بِتَكَرُّرِ الْخَرَاجِ فِي سَنَةٍ لأَنَّ عُمَرَ لَمْ يُوَقِّقَهُ مُكَرَّر بِخِلَافِ الْعُشْرِأُ نَّهُ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ عُشُرًا إِلَّا بِوُجُوبِهِ فِي كُلّ خَارِج
ترجمه ولا يتكرر الخ اور ایک ہی سال میں زمین میں دوبار پیداوار ہو جانے سے دوبارہ خراج نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے خراج دوبارہ مقرر نہیں کیا تھا۔ برخلاف عشر کے کیونکہ عشر اسی وقت لازم آئے گا کہ اس زمین کی پیداوار سے دسواں حصہ لیا جائے ۔ تاکہ زمین میں جتنی پیداوار ہوئی ہے اس میں سے دسواں حصہ لینا ثابت ہو ۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم
And kharaj is not repeated by the repetition of produce in a year, because 'Umar did not fix it as repeated, unlike 'ushr, because 'ushr is only realized by its obligation on every produce. Translation: 'Kharaj is not repeated with repeated produce in a year; because 'Umar did not fix it repeatedly. Unlike 'ushr, which is binding only by taking one-tenth of the produce, so that for every harvest one-tenth is taken. And Allah knows best.'
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from Kitab al-Siyar (Book of Jihad) regarding the nature of kharaj (land tax). The text states that if land produces multiple harvests in a single year, kharaj is not levied multiple times; it is a fixed annual obligation. The proof is the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (ra), who did not establish kharaj as a recurring tax per harvest. This contrasts with 'ushr (tithes), which applies to every harvest individually, as 'ushr is a proportional share of actual produce. The commentator explains that kharaj is based on estimated productive capacity, not actual yield, hence its annual fixity. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi understanding that kharaj is a land tax tied to the land's potential, while 'ushr is a crop tax tied to actual growth. The lesson highlights the practical difference: a farmer pays kharaj once yearly regardless of multiple crops, but pays 'ushr on each harvest.

Key Terms
الْخَرَاج (al-kharaj): A fixed annual land tax on conquered lands, not multiplied by multiple harvests.
الْعُشْر (al-'ushr): A tithe on each harvest from 'ushri land, repeated with each produce occurrence.
تَقْدِيرِيّ (taqdīrī): Estimated (as opposed to actual), used for kharaj assessment based on land capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kharaj not repeated when a land produces multiple harvests in a year?
A) Because kharaj is a fixed annual tax, not dependent on number of harvests.
B) Because the landowner cannot afford to pay multiple times.
C) Because 'Umar forbade taking more than one kharaj per year.
D) Because kharaj is only due on the first harvest of the year.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a fixed annual land tax, not multiplied by the number of harvests in a year, based on the practice of 'Umar (ra).
