The Two Types of Jizyah: Agreed and Imposed
Classifying jizyah into two types and proving the first type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify jizyah into its two types and explain why the first type (bi al-taradi) is binding using the Prophet's treaty with Najran as evidence.

Core Idea
Jizyah fixed by mutual agreement is binding and cannot be unilaterally changed by the ruler.

This lesson introduces the chapter on jizyah from the Kitab al-Siyar. The author presents a fundamental classification: jizyah can be established either by mutual agreement between the Muslim ruler and the non-Muslim community, or it can be imposed by the ruler as a fixed obligation. The first type relies on consent, making the agreed terms inviolable. We will unpack the legal basis and implications of this first type, supported by the precedent of the Prophet's peace treaty with the Christians of Najran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Locate the phrase 'وَهِيَ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ' (it is of two types) and note the two categories: jizyah by mutual agreement (بِالتَّرَاضِي وَالصُّلْحِ) and, by implication, jizyah imposed by the ruler (mentioned later in the passage).
The second type is not elaborated in this passage but is introduced as a contrast.
2
Understand the legal basis for the first type
Analyze the reasoning: 'لانَّ الْمُوْجِبَ هُوَ التَّرَاضِي' (the obligator is mutual agreement). This means the binding force comes from consent, not from the ruler's authority. Therefore, the agreed amount is fixed and cannot be exceeded.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that contracts based on mutual consent are binding.
3
Analyze the dalil (evidence)
Identify the proof: the Prophet's treaty with Najran, where he agreed on 1,200 garments (حُلَّة) annually. This is a sunnah (hadith) precedent showing that jizyah can be in kind and fixed by agreement.
The hadith is reported in Sunan Abu Dawud and considered hujjah (valid proof) despite a minor chain issue.
4
Apply the ruling
Conclude that any jizyah established by mutual consent is binding. The ruler cannot unilaterally increase or alter the terms. This applies to modern treaties or agreements with non-Muslim communities.
The second type, imposed jizyah, follows a fixed amount known from the sunnah, but the first type is negotiated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْجِزْيَةِ
ترجمہ باب ، جزیہ کے بیان میں جزیہ کی اقسام
كتاب السير
وَهِيَ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ جِزْيَةٌ تُوْضَعُ بِالتَّرَاضِي وَالصُّلْحِ فَتَتَقَدَّرُ بِحَسَبِ مَا يَقَعُ عَلَيْهِ الْإِنْفَاقُ كَمَا صَالَحَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَهْلَ نَجْرَانَ عَلى ألْفِ وَمِانَتَى حُلَّةٍ وَلانَّ الْمُوْجِبَ هُوَ التَّرَاضِي فَلا يَجُوزُ التَّعَدِي إِلَى غَيْرِ مَا وَقَعَ عَلَيْهِ الإتفاق.
ترجمہ جزیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ اس جگہ مصنف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے دونوں قسموں کو اس طرح بیان کیا ہے ۔ وَ هِيَ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ الخ۔ جزیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) وہ جو آپس کی رضامندی اور مسلح کے ساتھ ملے پا جائے تو اس کی مقدار وہی ہوگی جس پر دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا ہو۔ جیسا کہ رسول اللہ نے نجران والوں سے ایک ہزار دوسو (۱۲۰۰) کپڑوں کے جوڑے ( از ار اور چادر ) پر صلح کی تھی ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ مال کی موجب ( متعینہ مقدار جس پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہوا ہے ) وہ ان دونوں کی رضامندی ہے۔ اس لئے جس بات پر دونوں فریق میں رضامندی ہو چکی ہو اس سے پھر جانا اور تجاوز کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح و هِيَ عَلَى ضَرَبَيْن ... الخ جزیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) ایک وہ جزیہ جو مسلمین اور محاربین کے درمیان صلح و خوشی کے ساتھ طے پایا جائے ۔ جیسا کہ رسول اللہ نے نجران والوں سے سالانہ بارہ سو (۱۲۰۰) کپڑوں کے جوڑوں پر طے کر لیا تھا تو اس میں مصالحت کے بعد اس کی خلاف ورزی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اس وعدہ کو پورا کرنا ہوگا۔ واضح ہو کہ اہل نجران سے صلح کے حوالے سے ابو داؤد میں حدیث ابن عباس سے اس طرح مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نجران ( نون کے فتحہ اور جیم کے سکون کے ساتھ ملک یمن کا ایک علاقہ جس کے باشندے نصرانی تھے ) سے دو ہزار حلوں ( حاء کے ضمہ اور لام کے تشدید کے ساتھ ایک از ار اور ایک چادر کے جوڑے ) پر صلح کی کہ ان میں سے نصف تو ماہ صفر میں ادا کریں اور باقی ماہ رجب میں ادا کیا کریں اور مسلمانوں کو میں زرہ اور تمہیں گھوڑے اور تمیں اونٹ اور ہر قسم کے ہتھیاروں سے تمہیں تمہیں بطور رعایت دیں اور مسلمان ان ہتھیاروں کے ضامن ہوں گے (ضرورت نہ ہونے سے واپس دینے کے ذمہ دار ہوں گے۔) اس کے عوض لازمی طور سے ان کا کوئی گر جا توڑ پھوڑ نہیں کیا جائے گا اور ان کا پادری نہیں نکالا جائے گا۔ اور ان کو ان کے دین کے کسی معاملہ میں کسی طرح کے فتنہ میں نہیں ڈالا جائے گا۔ جب تک خود ان کی طرف سے کوئی نئی بات نہ پیدا ہو یا سود نہ کھائیں ابوداؤد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ حلہ کے معنی ایک از ار اور ایک چادر ہے ۔ اس حدیث کے سارے راوی ثقہ ہیں ۔سوائے اس کے کہ سدی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے شاید ابن عباس کو نہیں پایا لیکن حدیث حجت ہے۔ الحاصل یہ مال جو نجران والوں پر بطور صلح لازم ہواوہ جزیہ ہے جو باہمی رضا مندی سے طے پایا ہے اس لئے اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں آنے دیا جائے گا اور دوسری قسم جزیہ کی وہ ہے جو مسلمین بطور احسان ان پر لازم کر دے۔ جس کی مقدار مشہور ہے اور باقی عبارت کا مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
اماما
Chapter of Jizyah. Translation: Chapter on jizyah, its types. The Book of Siyar. And it (jizyah) is of two types: (1) jizyah that is imposed by mutual agreement and peace, so it is fixed according to what is agreed upon, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made peace with the people of Najran on [the payment of] one thousand and two hundred garments (hullah), and because the obligator is mutual agreement, so it is not permissible to exceed what is agreed upon. Translation: Jizyah is of two types... (explanation in Urdu). Commentary: ... (details about the treaty with Najran, the hadith from Abu Dawud, etc.). The conclusion: the wealth imposed on the people of Najran by peace is jizyah that was fixed by mutual agreement, so no change is allowed. The second type is that which the Muslims impose as a favor (or obligation) with a well-known amount.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on jizyah (poll tax on non-Muslim subjects). The author defines two types: first, jizyah fixed by mutual agreement (bi al-taradi wa al-sulh) between the Muslim ruler and the non-Muslim community. The amount is whatever both parties agree upon, and it cannot be changed unilaterally. The proof is the Prophet's treaty with the Christians of Najran, who agreed to pay 1,200 sets of garments (hullah) annually. The second type is jizyah imposed by the Muslim ruler on conquered peoples, with a fixed known amount (the text does not elaborate further here). The commentary emphasizes that the first type is binding and cannot be violated, supporting this with a hadith from Abu Dawud detailing the Najran treaty. The author also addresses the chain of narration, noting that although one narrator (As-Suddi) may not have met Ibn Abbas, the hadith is still considered valid (hujjah).

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): A tax levied on non-Muslim subjects (ahl al-dhimma) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
التراضي (al-tarāḍī): Mutual consent between the Muslim ruler and the non-Muslim community regarding the terms of jizyah.
الحلة (al-ḥullah): A garment set consisting of a lower garment (izar) and a cloak (rida'), given as payment of jizyah in the Najran treaty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for fixing the amount of jizyah in the first type?
A) The ruler's discretion based on the land's productivity
B) The capacity of the non-Muslim community
C) Mutual agreement between Muslims and the non-Muslims
D) A fixed amount set by the Prophet for all non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
The first type of jizyah is fixed by mutual agreement and is binding; the ruler cannot change it unilaterally.

Jizya by Mutual Consent: Binding by Agreement
States the ruling for jizya by treaty, citing the Najran agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya established by mutual consent and identify the proof from the Prophet's treaty with Najran.

Core Idea
Jizya by mutual consent is determined and bound by the agreed amount.

This passage introduces the first type of jizya in the Hidayah: that which is set by mutual agreement (taraḍī) and peace (ṣulḥ). The amount is whatever the two parties consent to, and once agreed, it becomes binding. The proof is the treaty of the Prophet ﷺ with the Christians of Najran, where 1,200 garments were set. The legal reasoning is that the obligating factor is mutual satisfaction, so no deviation is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The jizya imposed by mutual agreement and peace (bi al-tarāḍī wa al-ṣulḥ). The ruling is that it is valid (ṣaḥīḥ) and the amount is whatever is agreed upon.
This is the first of two types of jizya mentioned in the chapter.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the treaty of the Prophet ﷺ with the people of Najran as evidence that such an agreement is permissible and binding.
The hadith is a sound report (ḥadīth aḥad) but its meaning is decisive (qatʿī al-dalāla) for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
How does the treaty prove the ruling? The Prophet ﷺ agreed on a specific amount (1,200 garments), establishing that jizya can be set by mutual consent without a fixed upper limit. The command to fulfill agreements (Qur'an 5:1) makes the treaty binding.
The legal reasoning is that the obligating factor (al-mūjib) is the mutual satisfaction, so changing the terms later is impermissible.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilāf
There is no significant disagreement among the schools on the validity of consent-based jizya. This ruling is muttafaq ʿalayh.
The Hanafi position is from the ẓāhir al-riwāyah and is relied upon for fatwa.
5
Understand the legal principle
The principle is that contracts and treaties based on mutual consent are binding; they cannot be unilaterally altered. This is a core principle in Islamic law (al-ʿuqūd bi al-tarāḍī).
This principle applies to all bilateral agreements, not just jizya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَهِيَ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ جِزْيَةٌ تُوْضَعُ بِالتَّرَاضِي وَالصُّلْحِ فَتَتَقَدَّرُ بِحَسَبِ مَا يَقَعُ عَلَيْهِ الْإِنْفَاقُ كَمَا صَالَحَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَهْلَ نَجْرَانَ عَلى أَلْفٍ وَمِائَتَيْ حُلَّةٍ وَلِأَنَّ الْمُوْجِبَ هُوَ التَّرَاضِي فَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّعَدِّي إِلَى غَيْرِ مَا وَقَعَ عَلَيْهِ الِاتِّفَاقُ.
Chapter of Jizya. And it is of two types: jizya that is imposed by mutual agreement and peace, so it is determined according to what the agreement falls upon, just as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made peace with the people of Najran upon one thousand two hundred garments, and because the obligating factor is mutual agreement, so it is not permissible to deviate to other than what the agreement fell upon.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah opens the chapter on jizya and defines its two categories. The first type is jizya established by mutual consent and peace treaty. In this case, the amount is whatever both parties agree to, without any fixed limit. The proof is the treaty of the Prophet ﷺ with the Christians of Najran, which set the jizya at 1,200 garments annually. The legal reasoning is that the obligating cause (muʿjib) is mutual satisfaction (taraḍī), so once an agreement is made, neither party may unilaterally change it. This ruling emphasizes the binding nature of contracts and treaties in Islamic law.

Key Terms
جِزْيَة (jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state in return for protection and exemption from military service.
التَّرَاضِي (al-tarāḍī): Mutual consent between the Muslim state and the non-Muslim community to fix the jizya amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first type of jizya discussed in this passage, how is the amount determined?
A) It is fixed at 48 dirhams for the rich.
B) It is determined by mutual agreement between Muslims and non-Muslims.
C) It is one dinar per adult male regardless of wealth.
D) It is based on the land tax (kharaj).

Key Takeaway
Jizya by mutual consent is binding and its amount is whatever the parties agree to, as established by the Prophet's treaty with Najran.

Jizya Rates: Hanafi Graduation vs Shafi'i Uniformity
Presents Hanafi fixed rates for jizya by wealth class and rebuts Shafi'i uniform rate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi graduated jizya rates and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
Jizya substitutes for military service, so it varies by wealth — not a uniform head tax.

The amount of jizya imposed by the Imam on conquered non-Muslims who remain on their land is a matter of legal dispute. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the Caliphs and a qiyas on military obligation, adopts graduated rates. Imam al-Shafi'i, citing a hadith of the Prophet to Mu'adh, argues for a uniform rate. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the three wealth-based rates and their monthly/yearly amounts as given in the passage.
Memorize: rich 48 dirhams/year, middle 24, poor working 12.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
What uniform rate does Shafi'i propose and what is his primary evidence?
The rate is one dinar per adult male.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Examine the hadith of Mu'adh and its apparent generality.
The hadith includes women, which is unusual for jizya.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school counter the hadith and what is its own qiyas?
The hadith is specific to a peace treaty; jizya substitutes for nusra which varies.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in jizya collection between the two schools?
Hanafi: assess wealth; Shafi'i: uniform head tax.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ جِزْيَةً يَبْتَدِى الْإِمَامُ وَضَعَهَا إِذَا غَلَبَ الْإِمَامُ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ وَأَقَرَّهُمْ عَلَى أَمْلَاكِهِمْ فَيَضَعُ عَلَى الْغَنِيِّ الظَّاهِرِ الْغِنَى فِي كُلِّ سَنَةٍ ثَمَانِيَةً وَأَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمًا يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُمْ فِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ أَرْبَعَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَعَلَى وَسَطِ الْحَالِ أَرْبَعَةً وَعِشْرِينَ دِرْهَمًا فِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ دِرْهَمَيْنِ وَعَلَى الْفَقِيرِ الْمُعْتَمِلِ اثْنَيْ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا فِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ دِرْهَمًا وَهَذَا عِنْدَنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَضَعُ عَلَى كُلِّ حَالِمٍ دِينَارًا أَوْ مَا يَعْدِلُ الدِّينَارَ الْغَنِيُّ وَالْفَقِيرُ فِي ذَلِكَ سَوَاءٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِمُعَاذٍ حِينَ بَعَثَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ خُذْ مِنْ كُلِّ حَالِمٍ وَحَالِمَةٍ دِينَارًا أَوْ عِدْلَهُ مَعَافِرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ فَصْلٍ وَلِأَنَّ الْجِزْيَةَ إِنَّمَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلًا عَنِ الْقَتْلِ حَتَّى لَا تَجِبَ عَلَى مَنْ لَا يَجُوزُ قَتْلُهُ بِسَبَبِ الْكُفْرِ كَالصِّبْيَانِ وَالنِّسْوَانِ وَهَذَا الْمَعْنَى يَنْتَظِمُ الْفَقِيرَ وَالْغَنِيَّ وَمَذْهَبُنَا مَنْقُولٌ عَنْ عُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ وَعَلِيٍّ وَلَمْ يُنْكِرْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ وَالْأَنْصَارِ وَلِأَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ نُصْرَةً لِلْمُقَاتِلَةِ فَتَجِبُ عَلَى التَّفَاوُتِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ خَرَاجِ الْأَرْضِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ بَدَلًا عَنِ النُّصْرَةِ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالْمَالِ وَذَلِكَ يَتَفَاوَتُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْوَفْرِ وَقِلَّتِهِ فَكَذَا مَا هُوَ بَدَلُهُ وَمَا رَوَاهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ كَانَ ذَلِكَ صُلْحًا وَلِهَذَا أَمَرَهُ بِالْأَخْذِ مِنَ الْحَالِمَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهَا الْجِزْيَةُ
And a jizya which the Imam initiates to impose when the Imam has overcome the disbelievers and allows them to remain on their properties: then he imposes on the one who is evidently wealthy, each year, forty-eight dirhams, taking from them each month four dirhams; on the middle class, twenty-four dirhams, each month two dirhams; on the poor working person, twelve dirhams, each month one dirham. And this is in our school. And al-Shafi'i said: He imposes on every adult male one dinar or its equivalent, the rich and the poor are equal in that, due to his statement (peace be upon him) to Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen: 'Take from every adult male and female one dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir garments without differentiation.' And because jizya is only obligatory as a substitute for killing, so it is not obligatory on one whose killing is not permissible due to disbelief, like children and women, and this meaning includes the poor and the rich. And our school is transmitted from 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, and none of the Muhajirun and Ansar objected to them. And because it became obligatory as assistance for the fighters, so it becomes obligatory on a sliding scale like the land tax (kharaj). This is because it became obligatory as a substitute for assistance with life and wealth, and that varies with abundance and scarcity of wealth, so likewise its substitute. And what he narrated is interpreted as that was a peace treaty, and for this reason he ordered taking from the adult female even though jizya is not taken from her.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of jizya, which is imposed by the Imam after conquest when the non-Muslims are allowed to remain on their land. The Hanafi school specifies three rates based on wealth: 48 dirhams annually for the affluent, 24 for the middle class, and 12 for the poor but able-bodied working poor. These rates are from the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for a single rate of one dinar (or equivalent) for every adult male, based on the Prophet's instruction to Mu'adh in Yemen. The Shafi'i reasoning is that jizya is compensation for sparing life, which is equal for all. The Hanafi response uses qiyas: jizya substitutes for the obligation of military assistance (nusra), which varies with wealth, just as land tax (kharaj) varies by land productivity. Additionally, the hadith cited by Shafi'i is interpreted as a peace treaty (sulh) specific to Yemen, not a general rule, as evidenced by the inclusion of women in the command while jizya is not taken from women in standard law.

Key Terms
حَالِم (ḥālim): An adult male who has reached puberty; one who has had a wet dream.
نُصْرَة (nuṣrah): Military assistance; the obligation of free adult male Muslims to defend the state.
خَرَاج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land owned by non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on what basis does the jizya amount vary for conquered non-Muslims?
A) It is fixed at one dinar per head as per the hadith of Mu'adh.
B) It varies according to the wealth of the individual, analogous to military service obligation.
C) It is determined by the size of one's landholdings only.
D) It is the same for all adult males regardless of wealth.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi jizya rate varies by wealth because it substitutes for military service obligation (nusra), which also varies by ability.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Jizyah Rates: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on jizyah rates with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jizyah rates and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Jizyah in the Hanafi school is a graduated tax based on wealth, not a fixed poll tax.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the amount of jizyah imposed on non-Muslim subjects. The Hanafi school holds that the amount varies by the individual's financial capacity, while the Shafi'i school insists on a flat rate for all adults. Understanding this difference is crucial for appreciating how each school derives rulings from primary sources and how they resolve conflicts between different types of evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, clearly articulate the Hanafi ruling: the Imam sets jizyah at three tiers—48 dirhams/yr for the rich, 24 for the middle class, and 12 for the poor, payable monthly. Note that only able-bodied free adult males are liable.
The poor must still be able to earn a living; disabled or infirm are exempt.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Next, state the Shafi'i view: every adult (male or female) pays one dinar or equivalent, regardless of wealth. Their primary proof is the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take from every adult male and female one dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir cloth.'
The Shafi'i also argue jizyah is a ransom for sparing life, which is equal for all.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i proof. They argue that: (1) the hadith is specific to a bilateral peace treaty (sulh) with Yemen, not a general ruling, as evidenced by the inclusion of women; (2) the practice of the Caliphs Umar, Uthman, and Ali represents a stronger proof and was met with silent consensus; (3) jizyah is intended as support for fighters, analogous to land tax (kharaj), which varies by capacity.
The inclusion of women in some narrations of the hadith is a key indicator of its treaty-specific nature.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude by identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): under Hanafi rule, jizyah is a graduated tax assessed on wealth; under Shafi'i rule, it is a flat poll tax on every adult. This affects how the state collects revenue from non-Muslim subjects.
This difference is not merely academic; it impacts the financial burden on dhimmis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
۱۲۲
جزیہ کی تعریف
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم
وَ جِزْيَةً يَبْتَدِى الْإِمَامُ وَضَعَهَا إِذَا غَلَبَ الْإِمَامُ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ وَأَفَرَّهُمْ عَلَى أَمْلَاكِهِمْ فَيَضَعُ عَلَى الْعَبِيِّ الظَّاهِرِ الْعِلَى فِي كُلِّ سَنَةٍ ثَمَانِيَةً وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ دِرْهَما يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُمْ فِى كُلّ شَهْرٍ أَرْبَعَةَ دَرَاهِيمَ وَعَلَى وَسْطِ الْحَالِ أَرَبَعَةً وَعِشْرِينَ دِرْهَمَّا فِى كُلِّ شَهْرِ دِرْهَمَيْنِ وَعَلَى الْفَقِيرِ الْمُعْتَمِلِ التَيْ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمَّا فِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ دِرْهَمَ وَهُذَا عِنْدَنَا
ترجمہ وَجِزُيَةُ يُنتدى ... الخ اور دوسری قسم وہ جزیہ ہے جو امام المسلمین کا فروں پر بالکل ابتداء میں مقرر کر دے۔ اس وقت جب که امام ان کافروں پر غالب ہو کر بھی انہیں قتل نہ کرے یا غلام نہ بنالے بلکہ ) ان کو ان کی اپنی املاک پر باقی رہنے دے ) یعنی امام نے تلوار کی طاقت سے کافروں کے کسی ملک کو فتح کر لینے کے بعد بھی ان پر احسان کرتے ہوئے ان کو ان کے اپنے گھر اور جائیداد وغیرہ پر بدستور باقی رکھا اور سمجھ کے مطابق ان پر جزیہ مقرر کر دیا ۔ تو اس جزیہ کی مقدار شرع میں مشہور و معروف ہے۔ فیضع یعنی امام ایسے شخص پر جس کی مالداری واضح اور ظاہر ہو سالانہ اڑتالیس (۴۸) درہم مقرر کرے گا اس تفصیل کے ساتھ کہ اس سے ہر ماہ چار درہم لئے جائیں گے۔ اور درمیانی مال دار سے سالانہ چوبیس (۲۴) درہم جس سے ماہوار دو درہم کے حساب سے اور جس کے پاس مال جمع نہ ہو مگر وہ اپنی ضرورت سے زیادہ کما لیتا ہو اس پر سالانہ بارہ (۱۲) درہم (یعنی ماہوار ایک درہم کے حساب سے ) مقرر کرے گا۔ (خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ہراس خص پر جز یہ لازم کیا جائے گا جولڑائی کے اہل ہو۔ لہذا ایسے لوگوں پر جو اپاہج اور لیجے ہوں ان پر جز یہ مقرر نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ و مالدار ہی کیوں نہ ہوں۔ اور فقیہ ابو جعفر رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے قول کے مطابق مالداری کا اعتبار ہر ملک کی عادت اور عرف پر ہے۔ پس جو شخص جس شہر میں مالدار اور تو نگر شمار ہوتا ہو وہ قسم اول میں ہے۔ مع) خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ان تین قسموں کے اعتبار سے ہر ایک قسم پر مختلف جز یہ لازم ہوگا۔ یہ حکم ہم احناف کے نزدیک ہے۔
امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي يَضَعُ عَلَى كُلِّ حَالِمٍ دِيْنَارًا أَوْ مَا يَعْدِلُ الدِّينَا رَ الْغَنِيُّ وَالْفَقِيرُ فِي ذَالِكَ سَوَاء لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ المَعَاذَ حُدُ مِنْ كُلِّ حَالِمٍ وَحَالِمَةٍ دِينَارًا أَوْعِدُلَهُ مَعَافِرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ فَصْلِ وَلِأَنَّ الْجِزْيَةَ إِنَّمَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلًا عَنِ الْقَتْلِ حَتَّى لا يَجِبْ عَلى مَنْ لَا يَجُوزُ قَتْلُهُ بِسَبَبِ الْكُفْرِ كَالزَّرَارِى وَالنِّسْوَانِ وَهَذَا المَعْنَى يُنتَظِمُ الْفَقِيرَ وَالْغَنِى وَمَذْهَبْنَا مَنْقُولُ عَنْ عُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ وَعَلَى وَلَمْ يُنْكِرْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَحَدَّمِنَ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ وَالْأَنْصَارِ وَلِأَنَّه وَجَبَ نُصْرَةً لِلْمُقَاتَلَة فَتَحِبُ عَلَى التَّفَاوُتِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ حَرَاجِ الْأَرْضِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ بَدَلًا عَنِ النُّصَرَةِ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالْمَالِ وَذَالِكَ يَتَفَاوَتُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْوَفْرِوَفَلَّتِهِ فَكَذَا مَا هُوَ بَدَلَهُ وَمَارَوَاهُ مَحْمُولُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ كَانَ ذَالِكَ صُدْحًا وَلِهَذَا أَمَرَهُ بِالْأَحْدِ مِنَ الْحَالِمَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهَا الْجِزْيَةُ
ترجمہ اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہر بالغ پر ایک دیناریا جو اس کے مساوی ہو مقرر کر دے۔ اس معاملہ میں مالدار اور فقیر دونوں برابر ہیں ۔ رسول اللہ کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے جس میں آپ نے حضرت معاذ کو حکم فرمایا تھا کہ ہر بالغ سے ایک دینار یا اس کے برابر معافراد ( معافر ایک قسم کے یمنی کپڑے کو کہتے ہیں ۔ کسی تفصیل کے بغیر یعنی اس حکم میں امیر وغریب کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں فرمائی۔

۱۳۳
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل ذمہ میں سے ہر بالغ فقیر وامیر پر خواہ وہ مرد ہو یا عورت ایک دینار واجب ہوگا ۔ اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دوسری دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ جزیہ تو قتل کے عوض واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس بناء پر وہ شخص جس کا قتل جائز نہ ہو اس پر جز یہ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا، جیسے نابالغ بچے اور عورتیں ۔ اب جبکہ جزیہ قتل کا بدلہ ٹھہرا تو فقیر اور مالدار دونوں کے لئے حکم برابر ہوا۔ ہمارا مذہب حضرت عمر و عثمان اور علی سے منقول ہے اور مہاجرین و انصار میں سے کسی نے ان کے خلاف اعتراض نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ جزیہ کو اس لئے واجب کیا گیا ہے کہ اس سے مجاہدین کی مدد کی جائے تو زمین کے اخراج کی طرح جزیہ میں بھی فرق رکھا جائے گا اور یہ اس واسطے ہے کہ جزیہ تو جان و مال کی مدد کے بدلے واجب ہوا ہے۔ اور اس میں مال کی زیادتی اور کمی کے لحاظ سے فرق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کے بدلہ جو چیز واجب ہوگی اس میں بھی فرق ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے جو حدیث روایت کی ہے وہ صلح کرنے پر محمول ہے۔ یعنی اسی طرح صلح واقعی ہوئی تھی۔ اسی لئے بالغہ عورت سے بھی جزیہ لینے کا حکم دیا حالانکہ عورت سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جاتا ہے۔ ابوداؤ دو تر مندی اور نسائی کروایتوں میں ہر بالغ کا لفظ ہے اور عبد الرزاق وابن مردویہ اور مرسل ابوداؤد میں ہر بالغ و بالغہ دونوں کے الفاظ مذکور ہیں۔ لیکن عبد الرزاق نے کہا ہے کہ معمر کہا کرتے تھے کہ بالغہ کا لفظ غلط ہے کیونکہ عورتوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب اس کی اسناد صحیح ہے تو اس دلیل سے اسے غلط کہ نا خود غلط اور ناقابل قبول ہے۔ بلکہ اس کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ حکم مصلح کے طور پر عورتوں کو بھی شامل ہے جیسا کہ بنی تغلب کی صلح میں
ایسا ہی ہوا ہے۔
تشریح امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دریں مسئلہ ہر بالغ ذمی پر ایک دیناریا اس کے برابر وزن رکھنے والا مال ( جزیہ ) مقر ر کیا جائے گا۔ اس امر ( مقدار جزیہ ) میں مالدار اور فقیر سب لوگ برابر کی حیثیت رکھتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام نے حضرت معاذ بن جبل سے فرمایا تھا کہ تُحدُ مِنْ كُلّ حَالِم وَ حَالِمَةٍ دِينَارًا أَوْ عِدَلَهُ مَعَافِرَ ( ہر بالغ مرد و عورت سے ایک دینا یا اس کے برابر معافر (یعنی کپڑے کی ایک قسم) لیا کر) ۔ چونکہ اس حکم میں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مالدار و فقیر کی تفصیل بیان نہیں فرمائی۔ لہذا ہر ذمی خواہ وہ مالدار ہو یا فقیر، مرد ہو یا عورت سب پر ایک دینار جزیہ واجب الادا ہو گا۔
امام شافعی کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جزیہ کا وجوب قتل کے عوض میں ہے۔ حتی کہ ایسے لوگوں پر جزیہ واجب نہیں ہوتا جن کا قتل کفر کی بنا پر جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ نابالغ بچے اور عورتیں وغیرہ۔ امام شافعی کی مستدلہ حدیث ابو داؤد، ترندی ،نسائی، عبدالرزاق ، ابن مردویہ میں ہم معنی الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے اور مرسل ابو داؤد میں ہر بالغ و بالغہ“ کا لفظ مذکور ہے۔ عبد الرزاق بقول معمر فر ماتے ہیں کہ بالغہ کا لفظ غلاط ہے۔ کیونکہ عورتوں پر جزیہ واجب نہیں۔ لیکن اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب اس حدیث کی اسناد صحیح ہیں تو اس دلیل سے اس کو غلط کہنا مقبول نہ ہوگا ۔ بلکہ بنی تغلب کی طرح یہ حکم بطور صلح عورتوں کو بھی شامل ہو گا۔ مشائخ احناف نے بھی امام شافعی کی استدلال کردہ روایت کو صلح پر محمول کیا ہے۔ بائیں دلیل کہ بالغہ عورتوں سے جزیہ لینے کا حکم ( اس حدیث میں ) دیا گیا ہے۔ حالانکہ عورتوں سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جاتا۔
احناف کا موقف بمع استدلال اجماع صحابہ مذکورہ زیر بحث مسئلہ میں احناف کا موقف مبنی برحق ہے۔ کیونکہ
1۔ ابن ابی شیبہ میں روایت منقول ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے مالدار ذمی پر اڑتالیس درہم، متوسط پر چوبیس درہم اور فقیر پر بارہ درہم کے
And jizyah that the Imam initially imposes when he overwhelms the disbelievers and leaves them in possession of their properties: he imposes on the one of manifest wealth every year forty-eight dirhams, taking from them every month four dirhams; and on the middle class, twenty-four dirhams, every month two dirhams; and on the poor laborer, twelve dirhams, every month one dirham. This is according to us.

And al-Shafi'i said: He imposes on every adult one dinar or what is equivalent, the rich and the poor being equal in that, due to his statement (peace be upon him) to Mu'adh: 'Take from every adult male and adult female one dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir cloth,' without distinction; and because jizyah is only obligated in exchange for sparing from killing, so it is not obligated on one whose killing is not permissible due to disbelief, like children and women; this meaning encompasses the poor and the rich. And our madhhab is transmitted from 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, and no one among the Muhajirun and Ansar objected to them. And because it was obligated as support for the fighters, so it is obligated variably like the kharaj of land. This is because it was obligated in exchange for support with life and wealth, and that varies with abundance and scarcity of wealth, so likewise what is its substitute. And what he narrated (the hadith) is interpreted as a peace treaty; therefore he ordered taking from the adult female, even though jizyah is not taken from her.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the amount and basis of jizyah (the poll tax) imposed on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state. The author first presents the Hanafi ruling: when the Imam conquers a territory and leaves the original inhabitants in possession of their property, he sets jizyah on them based on their financial capacity. The rich (those of manifest wealth) pay 48 dirhams per year (4 per month), the middle class pay 24 dirhams per year (2 per month), and the poor but able-bodied working poor pay 12 dirhams per year (1 per month). The Hanafis emphasize that jizyah is only collected from those capable of fighting, so disabled or infirm individuals are exempt regardless of wealth. The standard of wealth is based on local custom.

Then the Shafi'i position is stated: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that every adult (hālim, i.e., one who has reached puberty) pays one dinar or its equivalent, with no distinction between rich and poor. His proof is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed Mu'adh ibn Jabal to take one dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir cloth from every adult male and female in Yemen. Additionally, al-Shafi'i argues that jizyah is compensation for sparing the life of the disbeliever; since sparing life does not vary by wealth, the jizyah should be uniform. Conversely, those who cannot be killed due to disbelief (e.g., women, children, the insane) are not liable for jizyah at all.

The Hanafi response refutes al-Shafi'i by citing the practice of Umar, Uthman, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them), which was accepted by the companions without objection—this constitutes implicit consensus (ijmā' sukūti). Furthermore, jizyah is not merely a ransom for life but is intended to support the Muslim army (nusrah lil-muqātalah); thus it is analogous to land tax (kharāj), which varies based on productivity. Since the obligation of support through wealth and person differs by capacity, its substitute (jizyah) should also differ. Lastly, the hadith of Mu'adh is interpreted as a specific peace treaty (sulh) with the people of Yemen, not a general legislative command, as evidenced by the inclusion of women (from whom jizyah is normally not taken) in some narrations. Hanafi scholars consider the stronger position to be the one based on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and consensus.

In practice, this difference means that under Hanafi rule, jizyah is a graduated tax, while under Shafi'i rule it is a flat poll tax.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A poll tax levied on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
حالم (hālim): A person who has reached puberty (adult), legally responsible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how much jizyah is levied on a person of middle wealth per year?
A) 48 dirhams
B) 24 dirhams
C) 12 dirhams
D) 1 dinar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives jizyah rates from the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and analogy to kharaj, resulting in a graduated tax based on wealth.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Jizya Amount Established by Ijma of Companions
Historical ijma' proof for Hanafi jizya amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof for the specific jizya amounts and explain why ijma' al-sahabah is considered a definitive proof (nass qat'i).

Core Idea
The jizya amounts are fixed by ijma' of the Companions — a definitive proof that overrides contrary views.

The Hanafi school holds that the specific amounts of jizya — forty-eight, twenty-four, or twelve dirhams depending on wealth — are not arbitrary but rooted in the practice of Caliph Umar and consensus of the Companions. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents this ijma' as a definitive proof, arguing that the silence of the Companions and continued practice of later caliphs establish an incontrovertible ruling. Understanding this argument is crucial for appreciating how Hanafis use ijma' as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical event
Caliph Umar fixed jizya amounts in the presence of Companions. Identify the three categories: wealthy, middle-class, and poor, and their respective amounts (48, 24, 12 dirhams).
The passage cites Ibn Zanjawayh and Mughirah ibn Shu'bah as the source.
2
Establish the absence of dissent
No Companion objected to Umar's decision. In Hanafi usul, the silence (sukut) of the Companions in a gathering where objections would be expected constitutes tacit approval (ijma' sukuti).
Tacit ijma' is accepted by Hanafis as a valid form of consensus.
3
Note the subsequent practice
Uthman and Ali continued the same amounts. This demonstrates that the ruling was not a temporary measure but an established practice.
The continuity of practice strengthens the case for ijma'.
4
Conclude ijma' of Companions
The combination of original decision, absence of dissent, and continuity confirms ijma'. This ijma' is considered a definitive proof (nass qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
Ijma' al-sahabah ranks higher than qiyas and individual opinion.
5
Apply to the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute
Since ijma' is qat'i, it overrides contrary views. Therefore, the Hanafi position is preponderant (raajih) and the Shafi'i view is considered weak (marjuh) in this regard.
The passage explicitly states that Imam al-Shafi'i's opinion is 'marjuh wa hal nazar' (weak and deserving of consideration).

حساب سے سالانہ جزیہ مقرر کیا تھا۔ اور یہ روایت مرسل ہے۔
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم
- ابن زنجو یہ نے کتاب الاموال میں نقل کیا ہے۔ حضرت مغیرہ بن شعبہ سے مروی ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے صحابہ کرام کے سامنے مالدار (غنی ) ذمی پر سالانہ اڑتالیس درہم اور متوسط پر چومیں درہم اور فقیر پر بارہ در ہم جزیہ مقررکیا تھا اور کسی صحابی نے اس فیصلے سے اعراض وانکار نہیں کیا تھا۔ لہذا جزیہ کی مذکورہ مقدار اجماع صحابہ سے متحقق ہے۔ بعد ازاں حضرت عمر کے اسی فیصلے پر حضرت عثمان اور حضرت علی المرتضی نے عمل کیا اور کسی صحابی نے بھی اس سے اعراض و انکار نہیں کیا تھا۔ پس اجماع صحابہ کا اثبات ہو گیا۔ اور اجماع صحابہ نص قطعی کا درجہ رکھتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مذکورہ مقدار جزیہ کے حوالے سے احناف کا مؤقف راجح اور امام شافعی کا قول
مرجوح و حل نظر ہے ۔
He had fixed the annual jizya by calculation. And this narration is mursal. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Seven. Ibn Zanjawayh narrated in Kitab al-Amwal that it is reported from Hadrat Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that Hadrat 'Umar fixed the annual jizya on a wealthy dhimmi as forty-eight dirhams, on the middle-class as twenty-four dirhams, and on the poor as twelve dirhams, in the presence of the Companions, and no Companion objected to or rejected this decision. Therefore, the mentioned amount of jizya is established by the consensus of the Companions. Subsequently, Hadrat 'Uthman and Hadrat 'Ali al-Murtada acted upon this same decision of 'Umar, and no Companion objected to or rejected it. Thus, the consensus of the Companions is proven. And the consensus of the Companions holds the rank of a definitive text. From this, it is learned that regarding the mentioned amount of jizya, the position of the Hanafis is preponderant and the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i is weak and deserving of consideration.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a historical proof (dalil) for the Hanafi position on the specific amounts of jizya. The commentator argues that the amounts set by Caliph 'Umar (forty-eight for the wealthy, twenty-four for the middle, twelve for the poor) were endorsed by the Companions without dissent, and later Caliphs 'Uthman and 'Ali continued the practice. This indicates ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, which is a definitive proof (qat'i). The Hanafi school relies on this ijma' to determine the jizya amounts, and this passage presents it as a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's differing view.

Key Terms
اجماع صحابہ (ijma' al-sahabah): The consensus of the Prophet's Companions on a legal ruling, considered a definitive proof (qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
نص قطعی (nass qat'i): A definitive text with certain transmission and meaning, leaving no room for interpretation or ijtihad.
سکوت (sukut): Silence of the Companions when a ruling is made, interpreted as tacit approval (ijma' sukuti) in Hanafi usul.
راجح (raajih): Preponderant or stronger opinion, as opposed to marjuh (weak).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the authority for the specific jizya amounts used by the Hanafis?
A) A direct Quranic verse
B) The ijma' of the Companions on 'Umar's decision
C) A hadith from the Prophet
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi jizya amounts are established by the consensus of the Companions, which in Hanafi usul is a definitive proof (nass qat'i) that overrides contrary opinions.

Jizya on Ahl al-Kitab and Majus
Ruling on jizya for People of the Book and Magians with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya for Ahl al-Kitab and Majus and identify the specific proofs for each group.

Core Idea
Jizya is wajib on Ahl al-Kitab by Quran and on Majus by Sunnah.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding jizya. The matn states that jizya is imposed on both Ahl al-Kitab (Jews and Christians) and the Majus (Zoroastrians), regardless of their ethnicity. The proof for Ahl al-Kitab is the Quranic verse 9:29, while for Majus it is the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as recorded by Bukhari. Understanding this ruling clarifies the scope of jizya beyond a simplistic reading of the Quran alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imposition of jizya. The ruler is obliged to collect it from eligible non-Muslims. Determine the hukm level.
Hanafis classify this as wajib (obligatory) upon the ruler, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil for each group
Find the evidence for Ahl al-Kitab (Quran) and for Majus (Sunnah).
The Prophet's practice (fi'l) is a proof for Majus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Quranic verse indicate obligation? The imperative to fight until jizya is given implies that accepting jizya ends the fight, hence jizya is a duty.
The phrase 'hatta yu'tu al-jizyah' sets jizya as a condition for ceasing hostilities.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While Hanafis include Majus, Shafi'is originally did not. Recognise the dispute.
Later Shafi'is accepted the hadith; the dispute is historical.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi with no intra-Hanafi difference.
This is a settled ruling in the school.

Source Text

قَالَ وَتُوضَعُ الْجِزْيَةُ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ وَالْمَجُوسِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ الأية وَوَضَعَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْجِزْيَةَ عَلَى الْمَجُوسِ
ترجمہ اور جزیہ لازم کیا جائے گا اہل کتاب پر اور مجوس پر خواہ وہ عرب کے ہوں یا عجم کے اس فرمان باری تعالیٰ کی وجہ سے مين الَّذِينَ أوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ الآية یعنی اہل کتاب سے قتال کرو یہاں تک کہ وہ جزیہ دینے لگیں الخ ۔ اور اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ نے مجوس پر جزیہ مقرر کیا تھا ( یعنی مقام حجر کے مجوس سے جزیہ لیا تھا ) ۔ (رواه البخاری)
He said: Jizya is imposed upon the People of the Book and the Magians, due to His statement: 'from those who were given the Scripture until they pay the jizya' (ayah), and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) imposed jizya upon the Magians. Translation: And jizya will be required from the People of the Book and from the Magians, whether they are Arabs or non-Arabs, because of this command of Allah: 'from those who were given the Scripture until they pay the jizya' (ayah), i.e., fight the People of the Book until they pay jizya, etc. And because the Messenger of Allah imposed jizya upon the Magians (i.e., he took jizya from the Magians of Hajar). (Narrated by Bukhari)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is a ruling (hukm) passage. The matn states that jizya is to be collected from two groups: Ahl al-Kitab (Jews and Christians) and Majus (Zoroastrians). The proof for Ahl al-Kitab is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Tawbah (9:29). The proof for Majus is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who took jizya from the Magians of Hajar, as recorded by Imam al-Bukhari. The commentary adds that this applies whether they are Arabs or non-Arabs, indicating the ruling is universal for these categories.

Key Terms
جزیہ (jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslims living under Muslim rule in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مجوس (majus): Zoroastrians, treated as Ahl al-Kitab for the purpose of jizya based on the Prophetic practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A Quranic verse specifically mentioning Magians
B) The practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Bukhari
C) Analogy to Ahl al-Kitab
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Jizya is wajib on both Ahl al-Kitab (by Quran) and Majus (by Sunnah), establishing a broader scope than the Quran alone suggests.

Jizya on Non-Arab Idol Worshipers – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on jizya for non-Arab idol worshipers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi qiyas allowing jizya from non-Arab idol worshipers and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the general command to fight.

Core Idea
Jizya is permissible from non-Arab idol worshipers by analogy to enslavement – subjugation is the common cause.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i on whether jizya (poll tax) can be accepted from non-Arab idol worshipers (such as Hindus or Buddhists). The Hanafis argue by qiyas (analogy) that if enslavement is permissible, then jizya, which is a lighter form of subjugation, is even more appropriate. The Shafi'is hold that only Ahl al-Kitab and Majus are exempt from the general command to fight; all other polytheists must be fought. Understanding this dispute clarifies Hanafi methodology of qiyas and the role of 'illa in extending rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafis allow jizya from all non-Arab idol worshipers. Note the exception for Arab idol worshipers (only Islam or sword).
The matn says 'and upon the idol worshipers among the non-Arabs (there is jizya)'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that the general command to fight (Quran 9:5) is only exempted for Ahl al-Kitab (by Quran) and Majus (by hadith). Others must be fought.
The exception for Magians is based on a specific prophetic tradition.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the argument: the general command is 'fight them' (Quran 9:5), and the exceptions are limited. Therefore, for those beyond, the original rule of fighting remains.
This is a strict textualist approach, limiting exceptions to explicit evidence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that since enslaving these idol worshipers is permissible, imposing jizya is even more appropriate because both involve subjugation and preventing mischief (salb al-nafs / stripping of status). This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
The 'illa (effective cause) is the subjugation needed to prevent harm.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow jizya from non-Arab polytheists, so they can live under Muslim rule without converting. Shafi'is do not allow jizya; the only options are conversion or war.
This has practical implications for state policy in multi-religious societies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَعَبْدَةِ الْأَوْتَانِ مِنَ الْعَجَمِ وَفِيهِ خِلَافُ الشَّافِعِي هُوَ يَقُولُ إِنَّ الْقِتَالَ وَاحِب ِلقَوْله تَعَالَى وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ إِلّا أنا عَرَفْنَا جَوَازَ تَركه فى حَقِّ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ بِالْكِتَابِ وَفِي حَقِّ الْمَجُوسِ بِالْخَبَر فَبَقِيَ مَنْ وَرَاءَ هُمْ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ يَجُورا سر قَافُهُمْ فَيَحْرُزُ ضَرْبُ الْجِزْيَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ إِذْ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى سَلْبِ النَّفْسِ مِنْهُمْ فَا يَحْتَسِبُ وَيُؤَدِّي إِلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَنَفَقَتَهُ فِى كَسْبِه
ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ عجم کے بت پرستوں پر بھی لازم کیا جائے ۔ ( مگر عرب کے بت پرستوں سے سوائے اسلام یا تلوار کے اور کچھ بھی قبول نہ ہوگا ۔ ( اس میں امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا اختلاف ہے ۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ فرمان باری تعالیٰ وَقَاتِلُوهُم یعنی کافروں سے قتال کرو کے حکم کی بناء پر قال واجب ہوا ہے۔ لیکن قرآن سے ہی ہمیں یہ بھی معلوم ہوا ہے کہ قتال نہ کر کے جزیہ لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور یہ حکم عام ہے عرب ہوں یا عجم سب کو شامل ہے۔ لیکن اہل کتاب سے قتال نہ کر کے جزیہ لینے کے حکم کو ہم نے قرآن سے جانا ۔ اور مجوس کے بارے میں ہمیں حدیث سے معلوم ہوا ۔ اس لئے ان کے ماسوا بت پرست وغیرہ کا حکم اپنی اصل یعنی قبال کرنے کا باقی رہ گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بت پرستوں کو غلام بنانا جائز ہے اس لئے ان پر جزیہ لازم کرنا بھی جائز ہوا۔ کیونکہ غلام بنانے اور جزیہ وصول کرنے میں سے ہر ایک کام سے ان کی حیثیت اور شخصیت کو چھیننا لازم آتا ہے تا کہ وہ فساد نہ کریں۔ چنانچہ وہ کما کر
He said: And upon the idol worshipers among the non-Arabs (there is jizya), and concerning this there is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i. He says: Fighting is obligatory due to His statement 'And fight them' except that we have known the permissibility of leaving it in the case of the People of the Book by the Book (Quran), and in the case of the Magians by the report (hadith), so those beyond them remain upon the original principle. And we (Hanafis) argue that it is permissible to enslave them, so imposing jizya upon them becomes permissible, because each of the two (enslavement and jizya) involves stripping them of their lives? They earn and pay to the Muslims, and their expenses are from their earnings. (But from Arab idol worshipers, nothing other than Islam or the sword is accepted.) In this, there is disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i. He says that based on the command 'And fight them,' fighting is obligatory. But we have also learned from the Quran that it is permissible to take jizya without fighting. And this ruling is general, including both Arabs and non-Arabs. However, we have known the ruling of taking jizya without fighting from the Quran for the People of the Book, and for the Magians we learned from hadith. Therefore, the ruling for those other than them (i.e., idol worshipers) remains on its original principle, which is fighting. And our (Hanafi) proof is that it is permissible to enslave idol worshipers, so it is also permissible to impose jizya upon them, because each of the two actions (enslaving and taking jizya) involves stripping them of their status and personality so that they do not cause mischief. Thus, they earn and... (cut off)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage. The matn states that jizya is also imposed on non-Arab idol worshipers, with a disagreement from Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i argues that the general command to fight (Quran 9:5) applies to all polytheists, and exceptions (jizya) are only made for Ahl al-Kitab (by Quran) and Magians (by hadith). Thus, others must be fought. The Hanafi response is that since enslaving these idol worshipers is permissible, taking jizya is even more appropriate because both involve subduing them and preventing harm. The commentary explains that the Hanafi position relies on a qiyas (analogy) between jizya and enslavement, and the 'illa (effective cause) is the subduing of the enemy. This allows jizya for all polytheists except Arab idol worshipers and apostates (as will be discussed later).

Key Terms
عبدۃ الاوتاں (abadatah al-awtan): Idol worshipers; literally 'worshipers of idols'—here referring to non-Arab polytheists.

Jizya from non-Arab idol worshipers is permissible in the Hanafi school by clear analogy to enslavement, based on the common cause of subjugation.

Booty if Conquered Before Jizya Agreement
Ruling on the status of captives when jizya is not accepted before conquest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the fate of non-Arab polytheists and their families when conquered before a jizya agreement, and distinguish it from the case where jizya is accepted.

Core Idea
Conquest before jizya turns the entire population into booty — enslavement is the default when jizya is rejected.

This passage clarifies the consequence of military conquest prior to any jizya agreement. It builds on the previous ruling that jizya is permissible for non-Arab polytheists; here it shows that if jizya is not accepted and war occurs, enslavement becomes the result. Understanding this sequence is crucial for a complete picture of Hanafi jihad rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
What is the condition mentioned? 'Before that' means before a jizya agreement is reached. The conquest occurs without prior jizya acceptance.
2
Determine the ruling for the conquered people
They become ghanimah (booty) for the Muslims. This means their lives and property are subject to the imam's distribution.
The term 'ghanimah' here includes captives.
3
Extend the ruling to dependents
The women and children are also included. They are not exempted; they too become part of the booty and can be enslaved.
This is different from some other schools that may exempt women and children from enslavement in certain conditions.
4
Note the underlying principle
The permissibility of enslavement for non-Arab polytheists is the basis. The commentary explicitly links this to the same 'illa that allows jizya: jizya is an alternative to enslavement.
If jizya were accepted, they would be protected; since it was not, enslavement applies.
5
Contrast with the alternative
If jizya had been agreed before conquest, they would become dhimmis and could not be enslaved. This ruling applies specifically when jizya is not in place.
This shows the two possible outcomes based on the timing of agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِن ظهرَ عَلَيْهِمْ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ وَنِسَاؤُهُمْ وَصِبْمَا نُهُمْ فَى الجَوازِ اسْتِرْ فَاقِهِمْ
ترجمہ وَإِن ظهرَ عَلَيْهِمْ الخ اور اگر جزیہ مقرر کرنے سے پہلے مجاہدین ان کو فتح کرلیں تو یہ سب بت پرست رد عورتیں اور بچے سب مسلمانوں کی غنیمت میں آجائیں گے کیونکہ ان کو غلام بنانا جائز ہے۔
And if they are overcome before that, then they, their women, and their children are (in the category of) what may be used as slaves. Translation: And if the mujahidin conquer them before fixing the jizya, then all these idol worshiping men, women, and children become booty for the Muslims because it is permissible to enslave them.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that provides the consequence if non-Arab idol worshipers are conquered militarily before agreeing to pay jizya. In that case, they and their families become ghanimah (booty) and can be enslaved. The commentary explicitly links this to the permissibility of enslaving them, which is the same 'illa used earlier to permit jizya. This ruling reinforces the idea that jizya is an alternative to enslavement.

Key Terms
غنیمت (ghanimah): War booty taken from the enemy, which includes movable property, captives, and slaves.
استرقاق (istirqaq): The act of taking captives as slaves; permissible for certain categories of polytheists.

Key Takeaway
Conquest before jizya turns the entire conquered population into booty, subject to enslavement.

No Jizya on Arab Pagans and Apostates
Hanafi ruling and dispute with Shafi'i on jizya for Arab pagans and apostates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya for Arab polytheists and apostates, and explain the basis for the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Arab pagans and apostates are so severe in their disbelief that only Islam or the sword is acceptable — jizya is a concession for milder kufr.

The passage addresses a specific situation in the law of jihad: Who can be granted the option of jizya? Hanafis hold that two groups are too severe in their disbelief to be given that option: Arab polytheists and apostates. The reasoning is that their kufr is 'intensified' for different reasons, making the usual leniency of jizya inapplicable. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, especially regarding Arab polytheists, and the text provides the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the two groups excluded from jizya: Arab polytheists and apostates. The ruling is that the imam must not accept jizya from them; only Islam or the sword is offered.
This is a strict rule with no exceptions for these groups.
2
Identify the opposing school and its position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Arab polytheists can be enslaved, which implies jizya could be taken similarly. The Shafi'i view is that they are not excluded from the options of war.
The passage only mentions enslavement; the exact Shafi'i ruling on jizya for Arab polytheists may be broader.
3
Follow the Hanafi reasoning (dalil)
The Hanafi proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli): Arab polytheists witnessed the Prophet and the Quran in their own context, so their rejection is more blameworthy. Apostates knowingly rejected the truth after accepting it. This severity requires a harsher consequence – no jizya.
The dalil is based on the concept of 'severity of kufr' (ta'alluq al-kufr), not a specific textual proof.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i view
The Hanafi response restates its reasoning: the severity of kufr precludes jizya. Enslavement may occur after conquest but is not a pre-conquest option. The text says 'our response is what we have said'.
The response does not directly refute the Shafi'i proof but asserts the primacy of the Hanafi rationale.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In practice, if a Muslim army encounters Arab polytheists, Hanafis cannot accept jizya and must fight until Islam or death. Shafi'is can accept jizya or enslave them, offering a third option. This affects peace treaties and battlefield rules.
This difference has implications for modern discussions on jizya and non-Muslim citizens.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تُرْضِعُ عَلى عَبْدِةِ الْأَوْثَانِ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ وَلَا الْمُرْتَدِّينَ لِأَنَّ كُفَرَهُمَا قَدْ تَعَلَّطَ أَمَّا مُشْرِكُوا الْعَرَبِ فَلِأَنَّ السَّى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَشَأَبَيْنَ أَظْهُرِهِمْ وَالْقُرْآنُ نَزَلَ بِلُغَتِهِمْ فَالْمُعْجِرَةُ فِي حَقِيهِمْ أَظْهَرُ وَ أَمَّا الْمُرْتَدَ فَلِأَنَّهُ كَفَرَ بِرَبِّهِ بَعْدَ مَاهُدِى لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَوَقَفَ عَلَى مَحَاسِي فَلَا يَقْبَلُ مِنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ أَوِ السَّيْفُ زِيَادَةً فِي الْعُقُوبَةِ وَ عندَ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُ اللهُ يُسْتَرقُ مُشْرِكُوا الْعَرَبِ وَجَوَابُهُ مَا قُلْنَا
ترجمہ اور عرب کے بت پرستوں پر جزیہ مقرر نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح مرتد ہو جانے والوں پر بھی جزیہ نہیں ہے یہ لوگ خواہ عرب ہوں یا مجسم ہوں۔ کیونکہ ان لوگوں کا کفر بہت ہی سخت ہو گیا ہے مشرکین عرب کے کفر کی تختی اور زیادتی کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ خود ان کے ہی درمیان پیدا ہوئے اور رسول بنائے گئے ۔ قرآن مجید انہیں کی زبان میں اترا اس بناء پر ان کے سامنے اور ان کے حق میں بہت سے. معجزات ظاہر ہوئے۔ اور مرتد کے کفر کے بہت بڑے اور سخت ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس نے پہلے اسلام کی ہدایت پائی اور اس کی خوبیوں سے واقف ہوا۔ پھر اس نے براہ راست اللہ عز و جل سے کفر کیا۔ لہذا مشرکین عرب اور مرتدین سے سوائے اسلام یا تلوار کے تیسری چیز قبول نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ تاکہ ان کی سزا بھی سخت ہو اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک مشرکین عرب بھی غلام بنائے جائیں گے۔ جس کا جواب ہم پہلے دے چکے ہیں ۔ یعنی ان کا کفر انتہائی خراب اور سخت ہے اور غلام بنانا فتح اور غلبہ کے بعد ہوگا۔ اور گفتگو اس بات میں ہے کہ اگر وہ لوگ فتح ہونے سے پہلے ہی جزیہ دینا قبول کریں تو قبول نہ ہو گا۔
And jizya is not imposed upon the idol worshipers from among the Arabs nor upon the apostates, because their disbelief has intensified. As for the polytheists of the Arabs, it is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was raised among them and the Quran was revealed in their language, so the miracle is more evident in their case. As for the apostate, it is because he disbelieved in his Lord after being guided to Islam and learning of its beauties. Thus, from these two groups, nothing is accepted except Islam or the sword, as an increase in punishment. And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, the polytheist Arabs are enslaved. And our response is what we have said. Translation: And jizya will not be fixed upon the Arab idol worshipers. Similarly, upon apostates, whether they are Arabs or non-Arabs. Because their disbelief has become very severe. The reason for the severity of the Arab polytheists' disbelief is that the Messenger of Allah himself was born among them and made a Prophet. The Quran came down in their language, so many miracles appeared before them. And the reason for the apostate's disbelief being severe is that he first received guidance of Islam and was aware of its beauties, then he directly disbelieved in Allah. Therefore, from the Arab polytheists and apostates, no third option except Islam or the sword will be accepted, so that their punishment may be severe. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, Arab polytheists may also be enslaved. Our response to this is what we have already stated, i.e., their disbelief is extremely bad and severe, and enslavement occurs after conquest and victory. The discussion is about whether they accept to pay jizya before being conquered; it will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states that jizya is not taken from two specific groups: Arab polytheists (pagan Arabs) and apostates (those who leave Islam). The reason given is that their kufr is exceptionally severe. For Arab polytheists, they witnessed the Prophet among them and the Quran in their language, so their rejection is compounded. For apostates, they knowingly rejected the truth after accepting it. Therefore, the only options are Islam or the sword. The commentary notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and allows enslaving Arab polytheists. The Hanafi response is that the severity of their kufr precludes jizya; enslavement is only considered after conquest, not before. The key point is that jizya is a concession (rukhsah) for those whose disbelief is less severe, not for these extreme cases.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate, one who renounces Islam after having accepted it. In this context, excluded from jizya and given only the option of Islam or death.
مشرکین عرب (mushriki al-arab): Arab polytheists of the time of the Prophet, considered to have a more severe kufr due to the closeness of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are the only ones mentioned in the Quran
B) Because their disbelief is more severe due to the Prophet being among them
C) Because they are wealthier
D) Because they are always at war

Key Takeaway
According to Hanafis, Arab polytheists and apostates are so severe in their disbelief that only Islam or the sword is acceptable; jizya is not an option.

Booty from Arab Polytheists and Apostates
Ruling on booty from Arab polytheists and apostates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the women and children of conquered Arab polytheists and apostates, and explain the proof from the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.

Core Idea
When Muslims conquer Arab pagans or apostates, only women and children become booty — established by the precedent of Abu Bakr.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a specific ruling regarding the treatment of captives from certain enemy categories. The author provides a proof from the practice of the first Caliph, demonstrating how the uncontested action of a Companion can serve as a binding precedent in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the scope of the proof and the categories of enemies to which it applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State clearly what happens to the women and children of Arab polytheists and apostates when Muslims overcome them. The passage says they become part of the booty (ghanimah).
The phrase 'only their women and children' (فَإِنَّ نِسَاءَهُمْ وَصِبْيَانَهُمْ) indicates that adult males are excluded from this rule.
2
Identify the Proof (Dalil)
Find the historical event cited as evidence: the action of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq with the tribe of Banu Hanifah when they apostatized.
The proof is a Companion's practice (athar), not a direct Quranic verse or prophetic hadith.
3
Analyze the Proof's Authority
Understand why this action is considered a valid proof in Hanafi usul. It was done by the Caliph in the presence of many Companions without objection, implying tacit approval (sukuti ijma).
In Hanafi fiqh, the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs is a source of law under certain conditions.
4
Determine the Scope of the Ruling
Note that the ruling applies specifically to Arab polytheists (mushrikin al-arab) and apostates (murtaddin). The proof from Banu Hanifah (Arab apostates) supports this, but the matn also includes original Arab polytheists by analogy.
This ruling does not automatically extend to non-Arab polytheists or People of the Book; different rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهِمْ فَنِسَاؤُهُمْ وَصِبْيَا نَهُمْ فَى لِأَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرِ الصِّدِّيقِ اسْتَرَقَ نِسْوانَ بَنِي حَنِيفَةً وَصِبْيَا نَهُمْ لَمَّا ارْتَدُّوا وَقَسَّمَهُمْ بَيْنَ الْغَانِمِينَ
ترجمہ .... اور جب مومنین مشرکین عرب یا مرتدوں پر قابو پالیں تو فقط ان کی عورتیں اور بچے مال غنیمت ہوں گے کیونکہ حضرت ابوبکر صدیق نے بنو حنیفہ کے مرتدوں کی ساری عورتوں اور سارے بچوں کو غنیمت کے طور پر تقسیم کر دیا۔
And when they are overcome, then their women and children are (in booty) because Abu Bakr al-Siddiq enslaved the women of Banu Hanifah and their children when they apostatized, and distributed them among the combatants. Translation: And when the believers gain control over Arab polytheists or apostates, then only their women and children become booty because Hadrat Abu Bakr al-Siddiq distributed all the women and children of the apostates of Banu Hanifah as booty.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a ruling with a proof from the practice of the first Caliph, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The matn states that when Muslims conquer Arab polytheists or apostates, the women and children become booty (ghanimah). The proof is that Abu Bakr did this with the tribe of Banu Hanifah, who had apostatized after the Prophet's death. He enslaved their women and children and distributed them. Note that the ruling only applies to women and children; adult males who are captured may be executed (per previous lessons) or enslaved? Actually the text says 'only their women and children become booty', implying the men are killed, as was the practice with apostates. This ruling applies specifically to these two categories of enemies.

Key Terms
بنو حنیفہ (banu hanifah): A tribe that apostatized after the Prophet's death; Abu Bakr fought them and enslaved their women and children.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A verse from the Quran
B) The practice of Abu Bakr with Banu Hanifah
C) A hadith of the Prophet
D) Consensus of all Companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that women and children of conquered Arab polytheists and apostates become booty is established by the precedent of Abu Bakr's treatment of Banu Hanifah.

Apostates: Killing of Men and Jizyah Exemption for Women and Children
Ruling on apostates and jizyah for women and children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on apostate men and explain why jizyah is not taken from women and children, citing the reasoning that jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting.

Core Idea
Jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting; thus those incapable of fighting—women and children—are exempt.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on apostates and the obligation of jizyah. The text establishes that apostate men who do not repent are killed, while women and children are not subject to jizyah. The reasoning is grounded in the nature of jizyah as a substitute for fighting, and those who are not capable of fighting are excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on male apostates
The text states that any male apostate who does not return to Islam is killed. Note that this applies only to those capable of fighting.
The killing is wajib if they do not repent.
2
Identify the ruling on jizyah for women and children
The text explicitly states that no jizyah is imposed on women or children.
They are also not killed or fought.
3
Understand the legal reason (talil)
Jizyah is wajib as a substitute for killing or fighting. Since women and children are not killed nor capable of fighting, jizyah is not due from them.
This is a causal reasoning: the obligation of jizyah depends on the capacity to fight.
4
Note the historical precedent
The practice of Abu Bakr with Bani Hanifah's apostates illustrates the application: women and children were treated as booty, not jizyah-payers.
This precedent strengthens the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کی عورتیں اور بچے مال غنیمت کے طور پر مجاہدین میں تقسیم کر دئیے جائیں۔ کیونکہ حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے بنی حنیفہ کے مرتدین کی تمام عورتوں اور بچوں کو بطور غنیمت تقسیم کر دیا تھا۔ یہ قوم مسیلمہ کذاب کا حال ہے جو رسول اللہ پر ایمان لایا پھر آپ کے مرض موت کے زمانہ میں اسلام سے مرتد ہو کر نبوت کا دعوی کیا۔ اور رسول اللہ کی وفات کے بعد حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے مہاجرین و انصار کا ایک لشکر حضرت خالد بن ولید کی سرداری میں ان مرتدین کے مقابلہ میں بھیجا۔ ان بن حنیفہ کی جماعت بہت زیادہ تھی۔ چنانچہ وہ لوگ ساٹھ ہزار سے زیادہ کے ساتھ لڑنے کو نکلے۔ اور سخت قتال واقع ہوا۔ چنانچہ حضرت ابودجانہ انصاری و نضر بن انس اور قراء صحابہ کی بڑی جماعت سب اس میں شہید ہوئے۔ پھر بھی اللہ تعالیٰ نے صحابہ کو فتح دی بالآ خر مسیلمہ کذاب مارا گیا اور بنو حنیفہ فتح کر لئے گئے ۔ تب آپ (ابوبکر) نے ان کی عورتوں اور بچوں کو تقسیم کر دیا چنانچہ حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہ کے حصہ میں جو عورت آئی اس کے پیٹ سے محمد بن علی پیدا ہوئے اسی لئے ان کو محمد بن الحنفیہ کہتے ہیں۔ یہی حال ان مرتدوں کی عورتوں اور بچوں کا بھی ہوگا۔
مرتد مسلمان نہ ہو تو قتل کیا جائے گا ان کی عورتوں اور بچوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہے
وَمَنْ لَّمْ يُسْلِمُ مِنْ رِجَالِهِمْ قُتِلَ لِمَاذَكَرْنَا وَلَا جِزْيَةَ عَلَى اِمْرَأَةٍ وَلَا صَبِي لَأَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلًا عَنِ الْقَتْلِ اَوْعَنِ الْقِتَالِ وَهُمَا لَا يُقتلان وَلَا يُقَاتِلان لِعَدْم الأهلِيَّةِ.
ترجمہ اور ان مرتدوں میں سے جو مرد اسلام نہیں لایا وہ قتل کیا جائے گا ۔ مذکورہ بالا وجہ کی بناء پر ۔ یعنی مرتدوں میں سے جو جنگ کرنے کے قابل ہو گا اس سے اسلام کے سوا اور کچھ بھی قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور کسی عورت یا نا بالغ پر جز یه لازم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ جزیہ لازم ہونا مغلوبین کے قتل کا بدلا ہے یا مجاہدین کے قتال میں مدد ہے۔ اور بچے اور عور تیں قتل نہیں کی جاتی ہیں ۔ اور نہ ان میں لڑائی کرنے کی صلاحیت ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا بچوں اور عورتوں پر جزیہ بھی نہیں ہے۔
Women and children are distributed among the mujahidin as booty. Because Hadrat Abu Bakr al-Siddiq distributed all the women and children of Bani Hanifah's apostates as booty. ... And whoever among their men does not accept Islam is killed, due to what we mentioned. And there is no jizyah upon a woman or a child, because jizyah is imposed as a substitute for killing or for fighting, and they are not killed and do not fight due to lacking capability.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on apostates and jizyah. It opens with a historical precedent from the battle against Bani Hanifah, where the apostates' women and children were enslaved and distributed as booty. Then the ruling is stated: male apostates who do not return to Islam are killed; no jizyah is taken from women or children. The reason (talil) is that jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting, and women and children are not killed or capable of fighting. This is a ruling with proof from practice and causal reasoning.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A per capita tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مرتد (murtadd): A person who renounces Islam after having accepted it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they are not wealthy.

C) Because they are Muslims.
D) Because they are slaves.

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting; therefore, women and children, who are not killed or fought, are exempt from jizyah.

Jizyah Exemptions for Disabled and Poor Non-Muslims
Details jizyah exemptions with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizyah exemptions for disabled and poor non-Muslims, identify the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes, and evaluate the evidence.

Core Idea
Jizyah is not taken from those unable to fight or work, even if wealthy – but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

Jizyah is a tax on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state, but it is not absolute. The Hanafi school exempts those who cannot physically fight or work to earn a living. This lesson examines who qualifies for exemption, the intra-Hanafi difference (Abu Yusuf), and the Shafi'i counter-argument based on a hadith of Mu'adh. Understanding these nuances ensures just application of jizyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify exempt categories
List the categories mentioned: the chronically ill (zamin), blind (a'ma), paralyzed (mafluj), and very old (shaykh kabir).
These are physically incapable of fighting.
2
Note the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling
The text states that no jizyah is due on these individuals. This is the relied-upon position.
زاهر الرواية
3
Consider Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that if such a person has wealth, jizyah is obligatory because they could potentially give counsel and be killed in war.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i opposition on the poor non-worker
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the absolute hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take from every adult one dinar.' The Hanafi response restricts this to those who can work (mu'tamil).
Inter-madhhab dispute.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi proofs
The Hanafi school uses the practice of 'Uthman ibn Hunayf with sahaba approval, and qiyas to land tax not imposed on barren land.
Dalil naqli and qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنگڑے، نابینا، مفلوج پر جزیہ نہیں
قَالَ وَلَا زَمِن وَلَا أَعْمَى وَكَذَا الْمَفْلُوجُ وَالشَّيْخُ الْكَبِيرُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ تَجِبُ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ لِأَنَّهُ يُقْتَلُ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ رَأَى وَلَا عَلَى فَقِيْرِ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ خِلافَ لِلشَّافِعِي لَهُ إِطْلَاقَ حَدِيثِ مَعَاذٍ عَنْهُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ عُثمَانَ عَنْهُ لَمْ يُوَظِفُهَا عَلَى فَقِيْرِ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ وَذَالِكَ بِمَحْضَرِ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ عَنْهُمْ وَلَانَّ خَرَاجَ الْأَرْضَ لا يُوَفِّفُ عَلَى اَرْضِ لَاطَاقَةَ لَهَا فَكَذَا هَذَا الخَرَاجُ وَالْحَدِيثُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى الْمُعْتَمِلِ
ترجمہ قَالَ وَلَازمين ... الخ اور ایسا لنجا جس کا کوئی عضو نہ ہو اور اندھے پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ یہی حکم فالج زدہ اور بوڑھے پھوس کا بھی ہے کیونکہ یہ لوگ نہ لڑتے ہیں اور نہ قابل قتل ہیں۔ یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ایک روایت منقول ہے کہ اگر اس کے پاس مال ہو تو اس پر جز یه لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسا شخص اگر لڑائی میں کم از کم مشورہ دینے والا ہو تو اسے بھی قتل کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور ایسے فقیر پر بھی جزیہ واجب نہیں ہے جس کی آمدنی اس کی ذاتی خرچ سے زیادہ نہ ہو۔ اس میں امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ ان کی دلیل حضرت معاذ کی حدیث ہے جس میں حکم مطلق ہے جو او پر گزر چکی ہے کہ ہر بالغ سے ایک دینار وصول کرو ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عثمان بن حنیف نے ایسے فقیر پر خراج لازم نہیں کیا جو کمانے کے قابل نہیں تھا یا اس کے ذاتی اخراجات سے بچتا نہیں تھا۔ اور حضرت عمرؓ نے تمام صحابہ کرام کی موجودگی میں اسے جائز رکھا۔ اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زمین کا خراج ایسی زمین پر نہیں لگایا جائے گا جسے وہ زمین برداشت نہیں کر سکتی ہو۔ اسی طرح یہ خراج یعنی جزیہ بھی ایسے شخص پر نہیں لگایا جاتا ہے جوا سے ادا نہ کر سکتا ہو۔ لہذا حضرت معاذ کی حدیث ایسے فقیر پر محمول ہے جس کی کمائی اس کی ضرورت سے بچ جاتی ہو۔
No jizyah on the crippled, blind, and similarly the paralyzed and very old, for the reason we explained. And from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that it is obligatory if he has wealth, because he is killed in general if he has an opinion. And there is no jizyah on a poor person who is not working, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who has the absolute hadith of Mu'adh. And our proof is that Uthman did not impose it on a poor person not working, and that was in the presence of the Companions; and that land tax is not imposed on land that cannot bear it, so too this tax; and the hadith is interpreted as applying to one who works.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses jizyah exemptions for disabled and poor non-Muslims. The main ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that jizyah is not taken from the chronically ill, blind, paralyzed, or very old – because they cannot fight and are not killed in war. Abu Yusuf has a contrary narration: if such a person has wealth, jizyah is obligatory because they could potentially be killed for giving counsel. The text then addresses the poor person who cannot work: Imam al-Shafi'i argues jizyah is obligatory on every adult based on a hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal (interpreted absolutely). The Hanafi proof is practice of Uthman ibn Hunayf (with approval of 'Umar and the Companions) who did not impose jizyah on such poor; also qiyas to land tax not imposed on barren land. Thus the hadith of Mu'adh is restricted to those who can work.

Key Terms
زمن (zamin): A person who is chronically ill or disabled, unable to move or work.
غير معتمل (ghayr mu'tamil): A person who does not work or earn an income; a poor person without means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for exempting the poor non-worker from jizyah?
A) A hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically exempting them.
B) The practice of 'Uthman ibn Hunayf with approval of the Companions.
C) Consensus (ijma) of the early scholars.
D) Qiyas to zakah not being taken from the poor.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi school exempts disabled and poor non-working from jizyah, restricting the absolute hadith of Mu'adh to those who can work.
